After the cure, wash the area several times with honey and other treatments until it heals properly.
de enfleure	To bloom
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling appears in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters but doesn't heal, then one should perform cauteries on the limb according to its size; and let each cautery go somewhat inside the hollow of the diseased area; then treat it with ointments until it heals properly. And whenever a new swelling appears at the hand or foot or back, along the exit of the nerve that paralyzes the limb, thus one extracts the swelling; and always no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about limbs and the exits of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of cauteries, instruct the patient to let their hair grow long and evenly; if they prick at their roots when young, hold them steady so they don't move until grown out.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" matures and medicine no longer helps, then one should use a small fire cautery according to the size of the spot, until the boil is removed and its color changes. Then apply cornmeal several times mixed with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood from chicken and blood from duck, each in proportion. Mix all together, bind it with a cloth, and leave on the affected area until healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of a sore by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the ulcer begins and you see it stopping, if you halt its progress by applying a cautery to the spot that seems like the first circle around the ulcer. And always, they say one should apply the cautery in the middle of the ulcer; and I always think this isn't good because I fear it might lead to inflammation and corruption. I've already decided against doing that several times; and a more correct method is to apply the cautery around its edges, using the cautery named 'circule', as we have described earlier when speaking about various types of cauterization.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it doesn't want to die, either due to its overgrowth or because of the old age of the illness when the body is too weak (meaning the person is very old), having little blood, or due to tension; then you see that it hastens towards death: in this case, apply small cautery treatments using several rounds; after that, leave them be. For it will hasten its own demise.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced through with all the cautery, heat the cautery as shown here:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" while both cauteries pierce through the head, and make sure both cauteries are such that the patient feels them going out to a degree where the process of decay is stopped. After treatment until it becomes completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another way of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing else than an infection of the body part because it eats away at the limbs like dry wood burns. If you see this disease in a limb that can bear heat, then heat up both the iron cauteries to be small and large according to what suits the limb where the illness is; after applying the cautery all around until you remove all corruption, leaving nothing behind, ensuring no remaining corrupted part remains. And then leave it for three days, and while the burns from the fire heal with oil, take care of any remaining corruption. After that, apply ointments that generate new flesh for three more days. If after three days there is no sign of healing, start applying heat to the infected parts again. And this disease can be cured in one go using medicine against fever instead of the iron cautery; however, iron cautery is more powerful aid. I have already explained the medicine against fever in its division: take it whenever needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of the roots coming to stones
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	There are times when stones cause a disease that we call 'clos' according to our understanding, and it is a large lump that irritates the foot. And for this illness of clos there are two ways of treatment. This means fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is that you heat one cautery like a feather from a goose, and make it out of good iron at the size so that it can envelop all sides of the nail, and ensure fine margins; after that place everything heated on the nail, and twist your hand around the nail completely until it reaches to the end of the nail; then leave it like this for three days until pus begins to form; then make a plaster from pounded wild marjoram mixed with oil, and leave the plaster overnight, and the nail will detach from its roots. Then cure the area with ointment until healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they have been turned inside out by the stone and it happens many times both in hands and in stones, then it is necessary that you apply hot water cautery; and here's how to do it: take a reed or iron rod, or a feather from a goose, place it on the nail and althelul, which means warts, and place the stick such that it touches all around, then put a little hot water, hold your hand well and twist your hand as the edge of the stick reaches to the root of the nail, and then find the hot water penetrates deeply until reaching the root; let the patient endure the burning from hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and all roots will be uprooted. Do another application in the same way until you remove all those who are within the stone, then treat with ointments that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shake due to cold or nerves, or a quartan fever or otherwise, it is necessary that you apply four or five cauterizations on the spine of the back. And one cautery between each vertebra; and one on the skin, and one under the stomach with the olive cauterization; if this continues to cause shaking, hasten his recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	puant sores
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	When visible through openings the body, or pus-sores that come from large corrupted matter, if it is necessary at first when they appear, to apply a fine cautery to each head of the pustule: a delicate faggot of myrtle wood, whose tip is taken by fire, or from the long root of aristolochia, or with the lenticular cauterizer. And never should it be burnt at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they do not grow out en masse, but their excess is dissolved which causes them, and are healed; but it should be done after bloodletting.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery has been cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times great variations of blood from the artery that has been cut at the wound come out towards the outside, or during incision of an abscess, or with the fire on the limb, and similar situations; it is a very vexing thing to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to any of you, if you quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it very tightly until the pulse subsides under your finger, and no drop passes anymore; then light several small and large olive oil cauteries until they are all red. Then take .i., or large or small depending on the wound and the location where the artery is located, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the pulse is fully congealed.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you remove your finger from the vein, and the cauteries are extinguished, take quickly another one of the cauteries that are at the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop performing this one after the other until the stump is completely burnt; and beware that you don't burn the nerve underneath, and that no harm comes to the patient; and know that when bone leaves the artery, it can be hard to properly reattach it yourself even if the artery is large, as long as it isn't treated by one of these four methods: through cautery, or extraction when not yet treated, or with strong string tying, or using medicines applied that have power to stop bleeding; and bind and restrain it accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer the reattachment, by tightly binding with cloths or placing hot things on, or other similar actions, if it doesn't benefit them.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have neither tools nor medicine at hand, should place their thumb on the wound of the artery as we have said, and stretch them out until they are completely burnt above the wound and above the artery; and don't move your hand but keep it moistened with cold water often while it is very cold until the bone becomes frozen, swollen, and burnt. And prepare to do the tasks that require cautery and medicines for this situation.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of treatments for amputations
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have spoken in the first chapter about every disease where it is necessary to use a fire cautery, or medicine that burns, and we discussed their causes, tools, forms of the cauteries; and I placed that chapter up until here, and I will go through this chapter using the same path so that one finds them more easily than before.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And as I start this, it must be known that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter of using the fire cauterizations, and for this reason, more caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and treating wounds, and extracting arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I advise you not to embark on folly. For many ways of people come into cures. Some come from those who are so affected by their illness that they die lightly due to the fear and panic they find in their disease, and the severity of their malice; and for these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And among these are those who give you their sense and say: "Wait, I am a coward"; illness is unkind. It is not fitting for you to agree with those who come to you in this manner, but place more constraint on your honor than on your covetousness, do not act rashly but wisely of those whom you are certain about, and of whom you can take and know; use prediction and guidance in the cures of your ailments that lead to health; and this will help you acquire good reputation, glory, and lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, Our Lords give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inspire by the holy inspiration of their hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have instructed you this chapter by considering it in parts, according to what is before or the section about cauteries that I have discussed up until the foot, so you will find it easier to understand for those who need it.
dou chief plein d’aigue	the head filled with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes so often in infants at birth, and when the mother holds the head of the infant too tightly; and it happens none of those times due to a cause that we know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never see this disease except in infants, and among all those that I have seen, it hastened their deaths; and for this reason, I think it is worth mentioning that I will divide the work into sections of treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one of their children the shoulder was full of water, and the head swelled each day until it could no longer bear it; and believed so much in the moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled around the bone in the syphac region, between the heart and the bone; and the veins are thus arranged when the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you cut a large gash through the head until it's wide; and so long as the moisture flows; and see this shape of the syphac:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, then make two cuts in a cross-shaped manner, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is around the bone, and you see the corners of the head opening from each part, and water spills out when you press it with your hand internally, and this does not stop: then it is necessary that you cut through the head in three cuts according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after making the incision, extract all moisture. After stopping the oozing from cuts and powders, apply wine and oil, and leave this manner for up to a fifth of days; then release it, treat the wound through changes and applications, and allow the head to heal similarly, and finally feed the patient dry meat from a small amount of moist until the limb is strengthened and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look where the opening of the abscess is large, and gather water; for it is not always in front; nor always behind; nor always on the right; nor always on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore cut where the abscess is open, and fill with water, and make a wound according to what you can do; and be careful not to cut the artery; and watch for blood flow, so that the patient dies from the bleeding and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	In reference to cautery using fire, command the patient to allow hair growth until it becomes long and uniform; if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they fully grow.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it comes to any illness that is called 'catarrh' in the eyes or at the bottom of the nose and such diseases are old, and the cure from medicine doesn't bring benefit, then the final treatment includes cauterization along with cutting off the two main arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you cover the eyes, let the illness operate behind the head; after this, rub the area with a coarse cloth until the arteries are visible, then pull out the illness's neck to both sides using one cloth. Then look where the vein lies and check the positions of both eyes from front and back after the ears, ensuring they have returned to normal; then mark both eyes with lime, then cover each one with a sharp knife blade up to bone for two parts, making sure it goes along the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, pinch off the sperm on both sides of the artery and vein above, cut them also as two inches through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the veins are incised, let the blood flow out continuously from up high.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open upon feeling it, you should measure the length of the space as three inches and then cut until you reach the bone; and what needs to be taken out of the blood is about seven parts per cent, and by chance a little more or less according to how the patient can endure it and the filling of the artery. Then look at the wound: if there remains a point close to syphilis under it, or if our incision does not reach that point, then heal the wound and bind it, and apply the salve until it is healed.

Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old age arrives, and severe coughing comes along, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples and elsewhere throughout one's aging body, as well as similar things. The treatment is done through ways of medicine cure techniques and all such methods do not benefit it fully; we would extract the arteries in the temples and cauterize them, just like what we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is such that the patient feels through their temple hairs, and listens to the artery opening at the temple, for it opens well by its pulsation, and responds only in some who are too cold; and if it responds, then strangle your neck with a few cloths, then rub the area with a hard cloth, and raise the area with hot water until the artery clearly appears. Then take the sponge that has this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then slightly peel the skin until you see the artery, then pull it up with forceps, and remove well any membranes that are off from each part; and if the artery is subtle, then turn it at the tip of the little finger. Then cover that part according to the size of both shoulders. For if it isn't covered, then don't let anything cut everywhere.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the bleeding from these two places until this point. And if the artery is large, it must be tied with two threads of a thick silk thread so that there won't be decay before the healing of the wound and so that blood doesn't accumulate thereafter; then cut off any excess between the two threads at that very moment, and then, if you see fit, cauterize gently along the cautery cut until reaching the bone as long as the joints are cut. And this is a minor procedure, provided the patient does not have fever and they have a warm constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauterization is help to finish off the wetness; because it provides more effective assistance against wetness.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	When it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, one must fill the hole with old cotton and place well-made tents there; and once they are removed, cut them with dry medicines that produce pus and tents until the wound heals; and if you don't have access to this, cauterize along this cautery trenching in two parts, but ensure the trenches are well spaced to allow heat to last longer. If you do not have this available now, put your tool inside as long as the tent is frozen, and remove it with cold water until the tent stops, and apply according to what is necessary; and that which is minor and more suitable for extracting arteries is when you cauterize along this cautery trenching in two parts, but ensure the trenches are well spaced to allow heat to last longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they hold less of their heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two knives, one should have a large gap. And when you intend to heat both ends, and place the hot iron until it reaches up to the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and let them be distant from each other among the two shoulders because there is no welding of this cautery everywhere; and this is how the cautery should look:
des larmes	Of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are draining through the veins that lie under the nose of the head of strength, and medicine cure doesn't prove useful, and you see the skin turn red due to this, and feel heat on your forehead as if there's a pulse; and wherever they are damp and moist such that paper hairs fall out, and the papers are heated, and scorched by the heat of the tears, then it requires this remedy.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called the old "bruise healer", and you should instruct the patient who has this disease to grow hair on their forehead, then make him three slits or cuts evenly across the forehead according to its length; and let one of these cuts be as two in going along the entire front until it reaches halfway up to the eyebrow, and the others two each at the ribs above the eyes, and keep clear of the incision of the arteries that are above the eyes; and keep your hand away from the continuity of the two jaws, and let each wound have the size of three in going through the joints;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have a piece of sponge ready and soak it in cloth to wipe away the blood, then apply the sharp wound dressing from two parts where this is formed:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	After the incision made behind the temple up to the second incision; and scrape off all the bone in between the two cuts right down to the bony surface. Then make another cut from halfway through this incision up to the other second one, and then extract that dressing.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you insert a tool in the first crack that is called "cultellaire", and it has sharpness on one side, and on the other side it is hard, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the tool cutting towards the inner skin of the ear, and the hard part towards the bone, and insert the tool until it reaches halfway through. And remove all vessels that descend from the head to the bones up until the continuous incision meets what opens into the ear canal, and then continue further in the middle crack until reaching the other opening; and remove blood evenly, and express the wound for the taken blood; then place a patch of old cotton in each crack, and place cloths soaked with wine and oil and vinegar above it, and ensure that no pus comes out; and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and apply a large amount of water dressing, then administer treatment with basilic ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it heals.
dou reume des eulz	from the pus of the bones
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When it comes to severe and recurrent fevers, and you see the eyes tired and small, and weakening of sight, and burned paper; and the hair falls out, and one sweats profusely in chills, and the body experiences external pain, then by these events you should know that those substances and that fever do not come from many veins, and with this treatment method, it is as follows.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And thus you instruct the patient to look behind their forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one wide. Begin from the left temple incision to the right temple incision, and when this cut reaches the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that move with chewing; once the bone is exposed, drain all the blood using a sponge, then clean between the two lips of the incision and place old cotton and linen cloth. Then cover it with cloths soaked in wine and oil, while avoiding to cause an abscess; when it has been removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until cartilage begins to grow, then treat it with desiccating substances, as they quicken cartilage formation.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of the oat flower and four parts of colofon, and make plaster; then administer it on these wounds to speed up cartilage growth everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the treatment of ear-sticking injuries
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that causes injury to the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or mine stone or similar thing like iron; or seed, like beans, peas; or flowing thing like water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it causes injury to the ear with a stone or any other thing that does not fit in the ear and does not grow in the ear, place the ear under sunlight. If you see the stone, if you can distill a drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then proceed with extraction; and have them sneeze out camphor, and when sneezing begins, stop up their nostrils, and put pieces of cloth or wool into the ear; and hold the ear above. Many times this treatment brings relief; and if it doesn't bring relief, then you proceed with extraction using fine forceps, which is described as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with forceps, that's good; if not, proceed with extraction using fine silk thread of small thickness; and if it doesn't come out this way, make a thimble from catgut or pull the end of the thread near the ear canal quite firmly, and stop up the space where the wick is in beeswax so that the thread cannot enter with the wax; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull forcefully. And many times this brings relief; and if it doesn't bring relief in such manner, then take the glue out and replace it with a tool suitable for this, and put some cotton inside; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if none of these things we have said cause her to jump out from all this, hurry to cut the ear in such a way that pus and blood drain away, and twitch; and the method of cutting is that you first make a surgeon's incision on the auricular muscle, remove some blood according to the measure of its strength, then let the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear where the fat hangs down; and let the cut be as round as a crescent moon until you reach the bone, then break the bone according to your power, and suck it rapidly into your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is gravel and it inflates, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer one small spatula tool according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And make an incision on that grain. But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to moisture in the ear, until you have made many pieces; then remove them with delicate tweezers and a suction tool, as we said before, so that the extractions become easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In hot water then, when the patient sneezes in the ear, instruct them to perform an expectoration of cold fluids and generously stuff the ear with old cotton. And lie down directly on that same ear where the heat resides. If it sneezes out forcefully through this method, that's good. If not, take multiple stones according to their length and softly place them in her ear; then heat each slightly over a flame; and place one or two pieces of these stones into her ear, and have her lie on the other foot from another side, and strike another stone against the stone inside the ear; and continue this procedure of one stone after another until all of the hot water escapes completely out, so it will all sneeze out completely. And if you notice, take a single reed, place the larger end in her ear, and light the other end with fire until the larger end of the reed becomes burnt; then repeat this process of different reeds until all the hot water has escaped, as we have explained for stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of small beasts such as fleas and similar things, treat it in the manner we have described for removal; but if they are of large size that can be felt, then perform the pinching extraction; and this is the easier thing to remove that is found inside the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms tangled in the ears, when you are treating it as we have described for divisions and distillations, and if the cure does not help, then you must examine the ear with the sun: if there is no worm appearing, extract them using fine pincers; and if they do not appear, take this form of sugar here.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And make it narrow below and wide above. And take the most subtle part of the ear according to the amount of suffering from the patient's illness, then apply this all over the ear; do this often until all the liquid comes out. And if they do not want to come out, you may numb the area with cotton like I have mentioned in the case of the stone; and if they don't protrude as we have said, administer distillations that the old ones have proven effective for worm cuts, and you will find them or a guide on distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, following this form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of silver or of tin with small perforations on the bottom and top for distillation; and to press inside the distillation use a properly made tool of tin suitable for this task. Take one piece of raveling cotton wrapped around the tip part, then pour your oil or juice into it, and let it be in the ear; then fill the raveling with all the cotton and gently press your hand until the oil is distilled or until some drops come out from the ear; and listen to the patient inside, and know that after such a distillation, the medicine should not be too cold because otherwise the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding ear piercing
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any intact parts in their ears; and this same thing happens to people due to wounds or birth in the ear, and these injuries happen inside the ear sometimes, if one cannot see them; and they happen only once inside the ear, when you can't see them. And they never occur twice, where one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which happens inside and cannot be seen comes from the injury of healing in various stages, and in this situation where one can see that you should place the ear under the sun; and look inside: if you see the evident swelling, if the work has become completely filled with pus as described here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be so that you cut in front and behind completely flat, so as not to irritate the ear; if the swelling is due to newly formed flesh or a bump of the ear, then use subtle pricks on it, and gently scrape it until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the pustules are in front of the ear, take one fine, light razor and warm it a little over fire, then place it inside the ear. If you feel the pustule that causes pain in the ear when touching it lightly, do so carefully not to injure the nerves in the ear; afterwards put into the ear a plug according to its size at the tip, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound heals or you take a plug and moisten it with rose water, and dust it with powdered vitriol. And if you see swelling in the ear, it must be that you remove the plug and put another one moistened with candle wax made from rose oil and beeswax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it's healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse an sponge and soak it in cold water, then place it on the ear, and perform other treatments that stop bleeding which include remedies for distillations.
de la char des papieres	From the substance of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	When handling wet and dry hairs in papers, it is necessary that you spread them using tweezers and forceps. Then, take a piece from its roots; afterwards, place sulfur on the part of the paper.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if you don't peel it off, cauterize it with a narrow lens cautery, and after the incision, it will start to move; and many times, there are no remains from its roots. And when they are cauterized by fire, those roots burn completely and never return.
de la gresle	Regarding ice or cold treatments
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times in papers, there appear some things that seem to gleam by their form and hardness, and because of this, this illness is called "granuloma", and it's a collection of large moisture on the surface of the paper. The operations are as follows: watch if the granuloma moves from one side to another, and this is a simple thing to know; do it then broadly, then lightly sear each part, then take them with tweezers, and remove them. If you cannot remove it without piercing a bit of the paper, or causing any harm to the patient; and if the rupture is large, and there's one seam, treat until it's healed; and if it's small, don't exert much force, because ointments will soon restore it and stimulate tissue growth.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granuloma descends into the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and place the granuloma under tweezers, then remove and press from both sides; and if the paper is moved by the incision, it does not harm anything; and when the granuloma has been removed, wash with salty water, treat the area that stimulates tissue growth until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the lumps
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Excrition is a kind of grease that gathers on the surfaces of paper, and this happens more often in children than adults, and causes much distress to their eyes, and they excrete tears during mornings, and cannot look at sunlight because tears quickly affect their eyes; and due to this, they lie with their heads on their arms throughout the day, sleeping while papers beneath them are damp from the excretion that opens in their eyes. And when you press your hand under it with your fingers and feel the excrement between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the process is that the patient places their head in your hand; and then take .i. linen cloth, and set up a tent in manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains excrement from each part, then put it on; press with your fingers on both sides, so that the excrement is gathered within the circle; then cut in the midst of the moisture with a sharp knife a groove wide, and not more than the wound when you open a vein; and let the leather be tight enough until you see the excrement from the groove, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then remove it all in one piece of thick linen between your fingers at the front, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed; and make sure you do not mix in the groove, that you do not reach up to the whole knife until it reaches the eye, that you do not hurt it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not open at the beginning of the cut, you should gently increase the cut size; then pull it as we have said. Then soak it in moist cloths and water, place it on the wound, and strain with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such people who grind meal and put it on to ferment the moisture that has remained. Then clean them as they become healthy. And if pus starts coming out at the wound, then treat with plastering until they heal.
des poilz des papieres	of the paper hairs
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow out of place and become old, they harm the eyes, causing diseases such as habitual tears and paper softening and albugine formation. These are reasons for eye damage; and treatment should follow these four methods: either by a fire cautery, or with medicine according to what was discussed previously in the chapter on cauteries, it can be done through surgery and stitching, or sutures, depending on what I will explain next.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the head of the eye in your good health, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is turned correctly, that's fine; if not, take one thread and sew it above at each end of the paper. Then do this along the edge of the paper where hairs grow beneath these hairs, sewing a single thread above across the whole paper, then turning it flat using a razor. Afterwards, cut through the part under the paper, under the displaced hairs, all the way from the large tear to the small one; then remove that thread and place a small cotton tent on top of the paper, followed by placing an 'H' shape figure on the paper, like a bay leaf. Indeed, it must be ensured that this figure matches the size you see when lifting up the paper which is folded over everything.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if it is necessary for this to require a large quantity of paper according to how the paper has softened; then make all across the surface of the eye drainage above the two lines you have marked, and start from the large tear until the small one; and if there are one or more tears close to the natural hairs in the thickening of about an inch, then place the needle in one of the corners of the eye socket, then scrape it all out. Then join the two lids together with a stitch made by hand using one thread of fine wool on both sides of the whole area, and clean out any blood, and let dry the excess threads above each eyelid where glue-like substances might accumulate if you see fit; and if not, just leave them alone for 3-4 days. Then treat the wound without stitches with drying and tightening substances, because the paper heals due to the adhesion of the wound and the joining together of the paper, but the stitch gets wet (as the old ones said), and it is an operation without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there's another way: and you sign the paper with a design that is as similar to the leaf of myrtle, as we have described, in 1.5 inches cut according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then, cut those that are above evenly according to the shape shown here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you are unable to hold the forceps and they aren't even, take a needle with two threads instead, and put it in the figure. et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And it is not the case that paper hair transforms; so you should use what we have said about incisions; but the stitches in one and another are more artificially done.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of canines follows this form: and you should convert the paper and cut inside according to what I have said, and then create four canines by art, and also two fine strings as long as the paper and as wide as the tip is; and place the tips of the two parts on either side; then assemble both finely above where the paper covers the eye, and tighten the two canine lines from each part formed; and leave it like this for a few days, and the skin that has been tightened will shrivel and turn black and spread, until it escapes by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes longer, and if the healing process progresses, then treat until it is healed properly; and when the wound has been stitched up, and if the paper lifts off, and hair will no longer grow; and this is the form of the two canines that you should create according to this figure, and in accordance with this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The surgical procedures are such that you need to take a fine needle, and attach one end of two thin silk threads to it. Then combine the ends together finely, making their lengths about a handspan long. Next, prepare another short thread of silk and tie the head to this thread. Proceed by placing the patient's head in the healthy position and ensure that sunlight illuminates everything during this process; for these are delicate and small procedures. Then insert the needle into all parts of the stitches at the base of hair until you reach natural hair above, performing this action swiftly on top of natural hair. Next, remove any hair up to the needle's location, and insert the natural hair into the needle if there's more than one or two hairs; then take out your hand ensuring that all hair is extricated from every part of the paper with natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the thread has been treated and no hair comes out with it, then pull the thread off at the other end until you've used up all the thread you have arranged. Do this until the thread is pulled out beyond what's normal and can be seen by your eye; thereafter, remove the thread and the thread itself, and close the cut for two or three days, until the hair returns to its place and grows flesh at that spot. And if the hairs are small, then accompany one long hair of natural animal with it, lifting it up together while you let it down, ensuring it's extended properly before lifting it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Regarding eye infection
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease, known as "aleacrati" or gangrene comes to the eye, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. It occurs suddenly from wounds, cuts by a tailor or cautery, and through similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the method of the operation in this is that you cut open that seam, and open the lips of it, and insert linen bandages inside, and bind them until it heals; and you must not use things in its treatment that dry out and restrict. For if you do this, the disease will return worse than the first one; but work with softening substances, like fenugreek; and soak water or boiled linseed oil and linseed seed oil into it, and apply butter to neither of the eyes, and wrap a linen bandage around it, and treat it with such.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you must be careful not to stitch it back together in the same form as before; and all these operations we have mentioned are only remedies for this disease, so that it does not return in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	The flow that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is called "axacrati" truly is natural and accidental. Accidents come from wounds, splits, cauterization, and similar things; and the path of this disease within it means you take a needle, which has two threads inside, and insert it into flesh. And the thread passes through the left tear duct as far as possible so that the threads lie in two parts of the flesh; then the flesh lies above all along the needle, and there is space for two small pieces to fit.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper figure comes out as it should, that is good; if not, take a razor and place it in the slit, then turn the paper, and make two slits inside the paper. And let the flesh of the two slits be at the corners of the incision you made, and make angles so that when they are assembled, the figure looks like a letter with two Greek strokes "γ". Then remove this flesh according to its size and thickness compared to the paper, then adjust the two removed parts symmetrically, using thread. Then perform the treatment of what we have mentioned about mollifying medicines and applying them until it heals.

And if the illness comes from a wound or stitch or cautery, it is necessary that you create an opening full of hair along the paper cuts, and according to what was mentioned previously; then cut between the two skin layers like I said; and must perform the operation according to the shape of the illness as they are very diverse in form. dou soudement de la papiere	immediately from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez. de la char sor le neis	from the flesh where the nose is.
