And if there remains any part we cannot correct, when you open the entire body with all necessary instruments gently and lightly, ensuring no obstruction; and if it's not obstructed or an abscess is sealed, treat it as necessary; and if it's an infected abscess, act quickly and cauterize until the pus is expelled and all flesh has been removed completely, then clean out with water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If it is the nose that's injured, and moisture leads up to the palate, know that it's healthy; and if moisture doesn't penetrate as intended, know that there was new flesh inside the bone, where the instruments didn't come through for cutting: then you must insert a thread of linen somewhat thick, and hold its ends with your hands, and place each knot about an inch or less apart; and lead the patient by this thread in their nose towards their mouth, and pull it gently until it comes out through their nostril; and many times do so when the children are at school, and it's a simple task for those who want to perform it; then hold the head that emerges from the nostril with one hand, and the other head that emerges from the mouth with the other hand, and distinguish them one after another by our presence. Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted that flesh, then remove the threads, cleanse the wound, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and place it back in their nose as before; do this for three days or longer, until all the remaining flesh corrodes away; and then use pine sap for several days if it's healthy, and if you need dried medicines, apply them; and this is the method of the instrument to purify the head, which involves distilling oils and medicines into the nostrils:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And make it of silver or copper, resembling an open lamp, like a rod, and guide it in the same way; and if you see fit, make a closed rod, and have your instruments filled to purify the head; and hold both ends of the head when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease is born near the nosehead, which is called "Telul", it grows and becomes large until one can see it; thus, at the beginning you should cut it, remove all bone, then place the fire cautery or hot medicine on it; if one delays cutting it until it's big, beware if it feels hard, changes color, has poor sensation: do not touch with metal as it's an infected abscess, for when one cuts once, it causes great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is due to heat touching, not just changed color, and you see that everything can be cut, let the patient remove and treat the area with drying and restraining substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose has been cut and sewn.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when the solutions of continuation reach into one of these venous conductions, they provide little benefit, in many cases. Therefore, it is necessary that this happen to no one, so long as their wound is fresh and full of blood; then adjust the two lips to a stitch, proceed with treating until it's healed; if the lips are already dry on both sides, you must cauterize all parts of them until they heal, then join the two lips together again, tighten them up, apply dragon's blood powder, and incense. And place the powders over a piece of plaster or another welding plaster, and leave it until it discharges naturally, then treat with ointment until healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of the stitch involves joining the material: either by needles, as we have said in the stomach stitch; or by thread, which I have previously informed you about.
des apostemes des levres	removal of lesions from lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the hands of one who knows, within the wound there is a hard part that resembles grains sometimes, both smaller and larger. So it must be that you return to the mouth of the wound and incise each node, then take them with tweezers and remove them from every part; after this, use the hand following the vitriol cut, until the parts are cleansed; then drain the liquid and cure the hand of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	from the pulp of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, a mass arises on the attached gum tissue, which the old ones called "albulus"; it must be that you hold it with forceps, cut it at its root, and leave out the wound or blood. Then place it under the vitriol powder, or other drying and desiccating powders; and if this mass returns after cutting, and many times happens again, then cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return even after cauterization; these are the forms of instruments to cut.
des sordens	Of cautering with fire, instruct the patient to allow hair growth until long and even; and if they pierce at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	In every instance they are gathered at the chief of the teeth, behind the mouth between the gums, and skin which is ugly and rough; and in each case the black tooth and citrine tooth along with worms exist until corruption reaches the gum, and then the tooth becomes stinky; it is necessary that you place the diseased person's head between your hands, and have their teeth or the scabs visible, until nothing remains; and do this for blackness and greenness, and yellowing and other colors, until they are all removed; if what was extracted was at first reason, it's good; but if not, then start again from the second day to the third, until you have everything removed; know that teeth require various tools of different forms to be extracted, according to how the work demonstrates it, for those who extract teeth outside the teeth have other forms than those who extract between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you are treating a tooth for its pain and delay the extraction as much as possible, it should not be done; because this is very rare. It must not happen that one removes too quickly because of this.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore when the patient is compelled to extract teeth, you must be certain about which tooth hurts. Often during pain from the tooth, you should ascertain if it's a tooth abscess and drain good pus; and in all cases do not depart entirely with the pain until the bad tooth has been extracted, as we have already seen fit for these soldiers; and when you are very certain about the tooth causing pain, it is necessary to sear around the tooth fully through i. spatumile strongly so that the gum remains intact from every side; then move it to your hands or to the fine tongs at each attempt, until they are well disinfected, then firmly secure the tongs; and keep the head of the tooth between your knees with the handle well in place, ensuring it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth straightly without breaking it, and if it doesn't spring back, take none of these tools and gently push inside each part, then move it as you did first. And if the tooth has been pierced and broken off, it is necessary to fill it with cloth at the points where they are; and when extracting finely with tongs, make sure not to break it during extraction; and it must be sharply opened around the gum in order to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And see that you do not break it or leave a part of it, and warn the patient about the increased pain from the root due to its malice after the first extraction. And take care that you do not act like ignorant soldiers who break it every time out of haste and rashness, and fail to follow what we have told; but they cause such illness once by the opening of this great disease through its roots or the bone they break, as we often want; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the inside with wine or salt water. And if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill that cavity with vitriol paste; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tools you use to pull out teeth should have long points and large handles. They should not bend when you are pulling on them; these are the desired shapes.
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them have large parts that do not bend when being pulled, and be made of very sturdy iron, and should have teeth to hold the pieces in place.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains during pulling, it is necessary to place inside the mouth cotton soaked in butter for one or two days until the gums are softened. Then remove the forceps called "algefri", making the shoulder appear like a doctor's beak; and they should also be made as smooth as a file, this is the desired shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the entire mass right up to the root, and then place an instrument known as 'althali', which is essentially an awl, as depicted here:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And make it so that neither breaks and is large enough that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps out from this, it's good; if this doesn't happen, assist with all instruments you have, as their forms are shown here after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if assistance is taken from the instrument that has two points, as depicted here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front according to the size of teeth, and from this tool which seems like large forceps, as depicted here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this tool not be able to break it, and know that very few of the tools are made of metal; and also other tools which are not counted; and the skillful surgeons themselves find their own instrument according to what their work and illness show them, because there are parts of diseases for which old teachings do not provide a tool due to their variety. If they break anything from cartilage or from the other bones, or if they rot, so they seek out the tools that suit him, as I have told you, and help with gestures, which is what this form represents:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well suited to hold the bone so that it doesn't escape but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with medicine suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, if you find all this tool:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form, and its shape is ugly, and especially in maiden women, you should know whether the tooth was born after it or isn't properly placed, and one can neither file nor grind it: then remove the groove; and if it's alongside the tooth, take this tool as shown here, resembling two small beaks, and let it be sharp at its tip.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the hole is made small and smaller in my hands by its hardness due to tooth, and because you do not move others, and if it becomes apparent that one can shave it off, then I will shave with one piece of file as this forms:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file used for making needles; and I gently shave in my hands slowly by tooth, so that it doesn't move until it's done; then make it completely flat with no rasp at the end. And if the edge is too sharp causing blisters on the tongue, it's necessary to shave off the roughness as much as possible, so that it doesn't blister the tongue or harm speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth swells
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth in front of the jawbone, or through percussion or impact, and the patients cannot press this upon what they eat that it does not produce feces, then you have cured them with medications restricting it; these are not effective so bind them with a gold thread as silver threads turn green and decay, but gold never changes. And use threads neither too thick nor too thin according to the space between teeth. Should you see the need for joining of teeth, take the thread and a pair of tweezers between two healthy teeth, then insert diseased teeth between the diseased teeth if there are more than one or several, until you can see properly up to the other side's tooth. Then resume the covering until it reaches the part where you inserted it, and pull your hand finely and skillfully, until it does not move. And bind your tie at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then clip off teeth with the thread using tweezers, then join them together, and place them next to a healthy tooth, make sure they do not irritate the tongue; and leave it like this tightly as long as possible, if it comes undone or breaks, bind it with another thread; should it continue in this state for all its time, this is how teeth are joined and the arrangement of two healthy teeth and two diseased ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth has shifted, should you set it back to its place, day by day as we have said; and do not interfere with anything that is not safe or endures suffering, and never make the shape of an osine's tooth, and place it in the spot where the defect exists, and bind it as we have said, so it stays there for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the tie of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	No once does it come from the glands situated on the tongue or in nature, that we are born with; or by accident due to injury healing; and the procedures consist of working within the mouth towards the ailment, having its head aligned with your healthy position, and lift the tongue; then cut out the nervous cord at length until the tongue is dislodged from its place. And if there is stiffness or swelling and it's due to sudden healing of injuries, then pinch the hook and cut at length that knot; and ensure that the wound doesn't become too deep down center because of blood vessel under it; and when you finish, raise it up in a pinkish-red or slightly swollen state, or in cold water, then place on tongue a piece of linen. And each night, wash this diseased person thoroughly, so that the tongues don't stick together. If bleeding starts occurring, then pour vinegar inside the mouth; and if that doesn't work out, then cauterize it with a slow burning cautery which is good for this purpose; then treat it further until it heals fully.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it is of any other color or blackness or hardness such that the patient doesn't feel it without touching, then don't touch it as it's a sore; and if it's fading towards whitishness, and there is moisture, then apply the hook until it gets cleansed and then cleanse from both sides; and if the pus fails to drain through your procedure, then pour vinegar over it until it stops bleeding, then proceed with your task until you exhaust all the means. Then raise it up using cold water and salt, and treat further until it fully heals completely.
des apostemes de la gorge	Extractions from the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	No matter how many times blisters arise inside the throat that are called "godath", and they're correctly named as the two almonds, whenever you treat them as we explained in separation, and if they aren't abscesses, then take caution: If these are small, tender, pus-filled lumps of a reddish color and with a needle-like consistency, do not touch them with metal. And if they are red and have a large root, avoid touching them with metal as well due to the potential for blood discharge; instead leave them until they're healed, then you will remove them, or they would dislodge by themselves; and if they are whitish in color, their roots are slender, then prepare your instrument to fit, but first ensure that these pus lumps have settled down and calmed. Then have the patient sit under the sun with their arms extended, and let their palms face towards health, and guide them to open their mouth while you press their tongue between their hands using all of the tool, in this manner; and use silver or finely made copper as delicate as knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue with all this tool? And when you see the pus lump, take the scissor and insert it into the almond, then pull strongly more than you can. Do not remove any threads, then cut using the tool; in this way it appears as a forceful process, that seems like pressing. Once the head is pressed from one place to another, it's very sharp, and made of iron or brass:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this tool now, take scissors instead; in this way it is formed:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make incisions on one side and the other; and when you have performed an incision in one of them, do the same for the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the sick person with hot water, or both cold and warm water, and if there is bleeding during the recovery, then gargle them with water or pieces of cooked cherry tomatoes, or leaves of wild rosemary, and similar things, until they stop bleeding; then complete the treatment as long as the body heals; and let no other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two glands, so perform the same procedure on them accordingly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was within her throat, one small in size. The entire throat had been so closely closed by it that she could neither breathe nor eat or drink through the blocked passage, and died after about one day or two due to this condition. The abscess was so far up that it had pushed aside two inches on each side of the neck. I acted quickly, inserting an inch of thread into one and pulled it out, with a large portion of the throat being exposed; then made another incision at the other nostril area, and opened her mouth forcing her tongue down; afterwards inserted the thread in these abscesses and removed part of them, only letting some blood come out. And thus cleared the passage in her throat, began drinking warm water and eventually wine again, not stopping until I continuously cut away from this abscess for a long time; it grew back immediately filling up the space that I had emptied completely, reaching quite large size. Then I covered these areas and treated them with a cautery inside her throat: she remained without growing anymore; I left those places, may God do something good of her afterwards.
de l’uve	Of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the urine comes out of the eye, and it is swollen and long, then it's called "perpendicular"; and if it's distended and round, then it's called "eye". When it’s treated as we have described in the division, but the treatment doesn't work, and you see that the incision from pus has healed and become subtle, then it should be handled; and this one which is round assembled and not long; and it’s red or yellowish or black in color, then it should be avoided with an incision. For there is great risk to the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to the way I have said, by its size and length, you must make the patient face the sun, and press their tongue onto the tool we mentioned previously; then insert the thimble into the eye, and pull it outwards, and remove it with one or two tools that I described in the incision of the two glands. And it should not be removed too much beyond its natural boundary; because if you remove more, it harms speech and language; and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the two glands, and treat until she is healed. And if your patient becomes afraid upon removing this one, then it must be handled with an instrument for cautery. The way to do cautery is by a sharp tool. And let that patient put their head into your healthy area, and then press their tongue onto the tool we said about in the chapter of cautery, and hold it firmly without being too thick or thin; and use the movement of this tool which has its form here:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have our head with a hair or we place the medicine on it, as if with the movements of a spoon, and put the tool onto all the medicine over the eye; and that patient should lie still on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth through the medicine inside, without reaching their throat and the wound; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on to the eye for half an hour, as long as you see it working and the effects of the medicine have subsided; and if you notice, take cotton and wrap it around any tool, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and place the tool onto the cotton in the wick above, so that the cotton burns on the eye; and do this often until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and rest for four or five days afterwards. And if you need to repeat the medicine cautery, then do so, and after the cautery clean around the eye with gauze soaked in butter, and clean off anything left of the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and gargle until healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, or rather the cautery; if it is treated with fumigation using this method, take valerian and sage and oregano and rue and chamomile and spinach and similar herbs, and combine all of them or some of them in one pot, and put them inside, then let it boil; and ensure that the pot is well covered with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot place two sticks according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And make it of silver or arsenic, and let one of the shoulder bones be placed in the mouth under the rash until the vapor rises to the eye via the nose, until the eye is dead; after that, repeat often, until the eye dries out. Make sure not to do this at the beginning of pus formation from heat, as many things can happen; and don't perform this treatment when the pus starts decreasing in heat. And if this tool isn't present, take a stick and place an eggshell inside your head so that the mouth under the rash doesn't get too hot; for the eggshell won't allow the vapor to burden the mouth, it is a good combined cure for healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it occurs in the throat bone or spinal area of fish, without any specific thing; so it is good that you remove whatever you can see and press your tongue against the sun with all the tool so that you see something move. And what doesn't reveal itself and remains in the throat should be induced to vomit out the rash until the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it escapes through vomiting; or if the rash ingests a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or half a piece of dry bread. And tie this sponge with one thread and then swallow it again. And when she comes to you, if she ascends, and then proceed to vomit. And if what we said did not bring it out, take one tool of snuff according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And make the tools curved at the tip so that they can more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted high above it; and guard not to touch the epiglottis, making sure no part of it moves or pushes any bone inside; and move such that the patient is forced to push the tool down because movement is necessary or if something is obstructing air flow; if they swallow it, or pull it forcefully until all parts are pulled equally out of the tool, as long as force is applied.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the windpipe
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No treatment of the windpipe has been done, as I have explained in division, through medicine therapy; and if this doesn't help, then look into the throat at the patient's complaint, after pressing their tongue with the tool I've told you about. And when you see the windpipe, pull it back by a little fraction of an uncia or use fine forceps that suit for this task. If this fails, take a thready hair and insert it in the throat at the patient's complaint; then pull until half the length of the hair is inside, and do so often. And if the patient smells water all day, take a full glass of cold water, work their mouth with it, pour it into their throat without swallowing immediately, and move it around frequently; and as soon as the windpipe feels the water, it will expel.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not expel as we have said, subfumigate the patient with aloe, using the tool I mentioned in the incision of the eye; do this many times for she will expel without any discomfort. And here's how to perform the fumigation: take one pot that contains charcoal sticks and place it covered with a lid in the middle, with an opening at its bottom where the tool's head is placed; then pour your fumigation, stick the end of the stick inside the patient’s mouth, seal their mouth so no smoke escapes but goes up until reaching the veins; and blood will now expel. If it does not expel, restart the fumigation several times; allow the patient thirst and consume salty things, do not drink water; then eventually she needs to leave forcefully through this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tool used to expel blood is such that when you can see it, it resembles curved scissors for cutting into the throat; and it has the appearance of a doctor's beak, and it has grinding roughness like a saw, so whatever she takes, she cannot let go. And here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	No descriptions of discharges are, according to what memory brings forward from one and another in this book, and they vary in perforation and in cutting; and this is done in two ways, one being in its own appearance, and due to the moisture it holds. And the second way is for the bones within the body. because abscesses on the head are different from those on the foundation, and abscesses on the inner flesh are different from those that come into joints, and each has their judgment in action.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if it's an abscess that shouldn't be pierced, as long as the body is healthy according to its completion; and for those ones which need to be pierced when they are matured, and don't complete their course of healing, such as abscesses beneath joints. Because when abscesses come beneath joints, if left until they are partially decayed in there, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint get corrupted, causing a contraction in that limb. Or it's beneath the main body part, and if you delay piercing until it is dead, it will harm the principal limb; or it's beneath the foundation, then pierce it accordingly when it is dead; and it should not be pierced an immature abscess without its digestion completion, except for the one that's beneath the foundation which doesn't rot all through, and stays inside, and produces a fistula; and can't heal properly in large scale.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time of piercing the abscess which is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the movement and sensitivity of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should have the piercing positioned above the abscess or as low as it opens, and where it appears; and make the piercing along the length of the body, and if the abscess is at the arms or legs, or joints and nerves and arteries, and all places where there's no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In cases where they bend, according to the same member. And when abscesses are within the fatty tissue, if you wish to move it, wait until digestion is completed and the puncture is confirmed, as we have said previously. For should you puncture it prematurely, the pus would spread throughout the body from the wound, filled with much filth; and might harden the lips or the deeper parts of him. And for any abscesses that are punctured across the broad part of the body, according to what the limb requires. And it is necessary to handle small abscesses with small pricks; and in large ones, large pricks, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and for those types where it's required to pierce through the bone, and cover them; when it becomes as thick as one piece of cloth, and has healed, then it is necessary to do so similarly to how you would handle milk blisters: and for those that are split into three angles, and for those whose handling is like the leaf of myrtle, similar to abscesses from angles; and for those where you make a round cut, and other cuts and shapes when they're handled accordingly.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those without a head, such as superficial abscesses, it is necessary to fully pierce them; and when the abscess is large, and has built up a thick wall, if you puncture it, do not drain all the pus immediately, but only some part of it; then cover the abscess until another day, then leave nothing directly over it; perform this multiple times from larger to smaller sizes, until all the pus is out; especially when the patient has weak strength or a woman in her pregnancy, young children, or elderly and decrepit people. For the spirits jump every time with the release of pus, that by chance kills the patient, and you might not notice it. Therefore, treat this chapter with great caution, and when you have punctured your abscess, if there's an opening, check whether the wound from the abscess is small; and if it's a full cut, apply linen or old cotton to it; and for large abscesses, and many wicks are there inside, it is necessary that you tie one in each so they stick together; and if you have cut into the abscess partially through the skin, and tied it internally, then fill it with old cotton or linen wads without moisture, and hold it until the third day; then dress it, and cure with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there's bleeding in your vein work, it is necessary to apply cold and moist cloth, and one piece of cloth, and place them on the wound multiple times. Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke and told of the art of cutting the throat; but I never saw anyone do it in our land, and this is written down from their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres. Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent loss from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we must make a cut in three or four small cuts across it, between the two circles or by the size of the cut's depth, not into the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And those lungs are suitable for the section of the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long under it.

dou chancre	and the sore

We have discussed in the division the appearances of gangrene and how to operate with medicine, as well as how to avoid iron treatment. We say that gangrene spreads when cooked meat is involved, and great caution must be exercised during treatment. According to old people, if there's gangrene on skin you can scrape it off like gangrene in breasts or in similar locations; and all of it should be removed at the beginning stage. If it's large and old gangrene, it shouldn't be approached as I've never cured any such case, nor has anyone been cured by me before.

de ydropisie	Of cautery with fire, command the patient to let the hair grow long and even; and if they prick at their root, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

The answer is yes, specifically those named tympanites and yposarche because they can be fatal. So when you're using medicine to treat erysipelas called "eclites" through medication, and the treatment doesn't show improvement, if you notice that the patient's condition is weak or there might be another disease besides erysipelas, such as stomach pain or similar symptoms; then do not apply iron, for it is uncertain. de l’estopement de la verge	On the operation to close the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	None of the times that children are born who do not have testicles, or whose testicles are small, or they are not in their place. If it happens to be so that it doesn't pierce through to both sides of a tiny soft spot according to this form: then put one thin metal ring under each testicle and secure them for about three or four days; and when it wants to urinate, remove the rings and let urine out, and then put them back again. And by chance nothing happens because the urine that comes forth doesn't leave the rings closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the testicles are small, if there is a medicine of metal rings of lead, as we have said, should they expand. de la piere des femmes	From the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stone occurs in women, and if it happens once, the treatment is difficult, and it's forbidden for three reasons: one reason might be that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second reason is that there won't be any woman who can reveal herself to lookouts, even when she is pure.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the fetus jumps, take its feet and push forcefully, then move its head upwards on the belly, then thrust your hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	And let the child grow slowly; instruct the woman to bear the pain until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the birth of the child which comes with one hand wide open
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It's necessary to engineer a way to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	If one cannot bring it back, then lift the woman and walk her around;

de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same manner for all the second part

adonques si istra legierement.	Therefore, if you treat it lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the issues of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or even four; this is not an uncommon thing, it just happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are exceptional things, and do not live long, if they occur at all.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know these, they are multiplied, and are removed by the fire that devises them, which is bound to the blood;

de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child

Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman who had borne an offspring that was dead, and then another one on him, and he revived the other.

Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, for this stomach has no bone.

dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the shoulder back to its place.

Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit. Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the second stage of labor is being retained during birth, it's necessary that you instruct the patient to hold back her urine, and then have her breathe through the nose with the aid of exhalation. Place your hands on her mouth and nose afterwards;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if it jumps over this, it goes well.

de percier lou fondement	of piercing the base

de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula near the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas coming from near the foundation are congealed and grow larger than those that come from further down or within the space of two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is a fistula or more than one; and when this lump is old, it may operate, and often produces moisture that appears white or thin.

And these fistulas are always present; and they can be identified when there is discharge or gustation during the patient's release, and by chance in their movement towards one side.

et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And it is that you bend your little finger or base, and insert a subtle needle of spider or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.

et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no full evacuation nor suction nor worm, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	you'll know that she isn't puncturing; so hasten to cure.

s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no twisting and the pain is contained internally, then it can be considered as being in a state of inflammation, and it does not respond to medicine or binding with a salve;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And for these internal fistulas, there is no effective treatment other than labor and the vain efforts of those who interfere.

des emorroydes	From the arrows.

dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	this means "by drying out or the ground" in modern English. The sentence seems to be part of instructions on how to dry something or set it on a foundation.

dou fremit	When the fire cautery instructs the patient to let their hairs grow long and even; if they prick at their base, hold steady until they fully grow.

et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And whenever the vein hardens, and one feels it as a death tremor, and it is sensed throughout the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.

de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the bladder

No single time is there use of silver or lead needles, or melted spiders; and no time are these small and large tools made, according to their intended use.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, when it comes to treating infants and those who are weak and in pain, they need small ones.

des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have spoken about the treatment of wounds in our previous sections; now we will discuss the treatments for hands and medicine according to their development.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various depending on how they were made, and where they were made on the body, and for what reason they were made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things through which wounds are made are by dint of stone, and size of sword and knife, or spear or staff or axe, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or those that are made according to the bones of the body, such as a wound that hits the neck, or the head, or the chest, or the abdomen, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and start with wounds of the simple head, because the memory will come to its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes or affects the head, and if no bone is broken, take care whether it's caused by stone or similar things, and the skin remains somewhat torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	And if you slightly doubt the abscess: if there is a slight amount of bleeding from the wound immediately after the operation on the cephalic part, then treat it as healthy in that area. Otherwise, treat the opposite side of the affected part instead.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	And let the patients be full of wine and rich meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if they do not want to be treated, then reduce their food intake, and do not give them wine nor meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	And over the wound, if abscesses are there, place a moistened cotton in oil rose water only, or in restorative wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	And if there is no abscess, place it on the wound, if it's fresh with all its blood, and isn't disturbed by the air, powder, that I will mention later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it has been burnt, place some remedies on it, as long as it remains intact.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword cut and similar injuries, and the edges cannot be brought together with stitches, then bring them together by suture, as I will explain for wounds of the abdomen, through sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound exposes the bone and is deep, retaining only a little, if you cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh instead of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And instruct the patient to consume large meats, such as testicles and cooked wheat, as well as chickens and similar items.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or smell decayed flesh, and it does not reach the bone, then cut out everything decaying, remove the pus, then treat;
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if it has an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicine, then cut out the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this doesn't help at all, then apply the cautery.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light: and you should apply this powder that heals in such a way that the heat of fire brings it to completion.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the method of the powder is as follows: take one part of incense; blood from a dragon .ii parts; living charcoal .iii parts, and finely powdered,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	And apply the wound with it, and press firmly until it dries well and joins with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And bind it properly, leaving it without letting it loosen, if it doesn't swell; for the medicine is not removed until it heals.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And always this is done with the charcoal alone, when one does not have the incense nor the blood of dragon, but when the art has healed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the art (healing) has healed the wound, in that case, do not add this powder either.
