et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And then a bit later, it spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then I realized that it was tearing inside the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved from limb to limb in this manner, for I had never seen such an illness conducted like this before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Still, I have seen many that would cause pain in their limbs to move elsewhere,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never witnessed this before, as I see it in the case of a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I wondered that this was due to the fact that her belly was swollen and her veins were exposed,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And because of this, there appears that constrained wind;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and does not appear according to this reason among those who are delicious and have moist bodies and veins that respond.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see the treatment of this disease, and if the patient feels pain, if it opens in the way that we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If it opens upwards and downwards quickly, then treat until that constrained wind at the body escapes;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	And apply a cautery to it; and if you cannot see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if you treat those who suffer from wind debility, like stinky pills, pills made of viper venom, and similar others.
Des saiettes	From arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearances and the locations where they pierce the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of them is such that there are those with large points, and small ones, and those with hair, and those joined.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those where there are pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and the one who defecates in no member, yet does so according to two ways: or within the main member itself,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	like the brain, heart, liver, stomach, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she gives birth then in no part of these limbs, and the sign of death that I will tell you later, becomes evident:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you have to remove this arrow, for death comes afterwards in various conditions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when that bad sign does not become evident and the arrow is not fully out, remove it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	The sign of the skull when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and jumps out from where it was in the head,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	when there is blindness and numbness and swelling of the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of thought, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes affects the nostrils or ears; and sometimes there is loss of speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	a white swelling at the wound resembling a boil, and also a burn like that from hot iron.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if you see this sign, continue with the treatment, and remove the arrow if it is not there already.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it pierces or hits the heart, is that it's close to the left breast, and also feels like it is stuck in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the arrow can also stop like a pulse, and brings black blood, and causes coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore, without doubt, know that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never leaves its wound is that without any foam spilling from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient's face turns a different color, and they sigh loudly with cold chills.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow stops within the thigh's cover, it hits the small bones; and causes great pain and intense agony and sighing; and all body parts from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow stops in the stomach or intestine, by chance if it breaks out of the wound, there's no undigested flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow stops in the belly or abdomen, and it jumps out of the wound not through the intestines, there's no hope for treatment, nor is there any hope for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow stops in the bladder and causes urination to occur, and leaks out, causing great pain to the patient: you know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other body parts, such as the limbs and neck and throat and shoulder and shoulder blade and back spine and ribs and arms and legs, and similar seeming limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerves or arteries and it's not poisonous, like what I will tell you, this happened to me because of what you were doing.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one and a half homes that an arrow hit or pierced the lung at its base near the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and I pulled it out from the other side through the fat of the ear, and there was no serious injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And take out an arrow, when it falls into the oil grease near the paper over the eye.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow had returned, and one could only touch its tip towards the shaft.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was large as an Ottoman bow, weighing just one fine feather without ears; the hunt was safe, and no ill accidents befell it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And take out an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and this is the Arab arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was grooming their eyebrows, and trimming them as long as I was doing it, and it pleased the Christians.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And pulled out an arrow at one's inch, whether from their back or belly, and I thought they were going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after thirty days, if it did not change its position;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and I aimed it, and pulled it out, and there was no bad incident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you find one arrow which has fallen or been shot through, and there is a wound joined up at that spot;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and wait until the arrow remains inside it, and do not disturb its natural positions,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor does it cause harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And observe another person, who has an arrow through their face and the wound is sealed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And let it endure like this to suffer great pain; and few other symptoms.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And pull out an arrow from the king's right arm for one and a half days during the service of the princes, as it was stuck in his left arm.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and had slightly weakened on the right side; and the arrow was completely inserted.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat it after three days when it happened. I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried very hard to do this but felt nothing;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and there was pain and discomfort in his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it might be from the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I placed an adhesive and digestive plaster on his head because the ears were not swollen;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And I saw the head of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the poultice to the wound for days, and quickly resolved the injury, then allowed the patient to rest for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	Until he felt the arrow within his nose; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied corrosive mercury medicine to the wound for days, until it opened up completely,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	And try it, and feel the tip of the arrow which was moving towards the shoulder;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then adjust it in the opening of the wound through this medicinal method, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and pierced deeply into the inner parts for a period of four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then I opened the wound so that my pincers could reach inside, and applied treatment from both sides, but couldn't remove it;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Therefore do not stop refining and devising ways for the tools, until I took one whole day using well-made forceps,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Following what its form comes to the end of this chapter, until I treat it, and will restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the judges decide that the cartilage at the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	So I treated it accordingly, and healed the wound, and was completely cured of the patient's ailments.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	And I told you about the quality of extracting some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that when you apply your method to what I don't say, because books cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters compare well on a small matter, and on that which is immediate and lacking;
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find nine works, and the new instrument, for the expulsion of things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not exist within the limbs where they are embedded, according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by their length where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And the one that jumps when it is at its length as it enters, this is an arrow entering into their flesh, and jumps without fail ever since.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump now, let her grow until the wound is properly healed from the inside out, and await the healing of the outside;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And similarly if it's stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, if she leaves her like that for a few days, and removes her each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it doesn't jump, she punctures through to the very center of the bone with a fine needle, until the inside of her elbow is widened, and then removes her.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone at the head, and goes up to one of the brain chambers,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and all the incidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: if she does not remove it immediately, but leaves it until its wound is equalized after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if the arrow reaches just to the joint, this is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow only penetrates through the bone and does not reach up to the joint,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and stays with no harm happening for some days without any bad incident, if the treatment has been done well.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is thus embedded and cannot come out like that, if you apply the arrows internally, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals properly.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is returned inside the body so it cannot be seen, one should seek it throughout the entire body;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, try to guide it with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot by the constriction of the wound, and due to the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then make an incision as long as the wound becomes large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has heads on the shaft she holds,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if the bone is embedded by two parts at the depth that you can reach,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as long as you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	do this carefully so that you do not break the arrow, making its extraction more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it in one go, till your arm is numb from the effort, then move on, because the extraction requires endurance.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the blood flow causes you to deviate, then apply what we have instructed about treatment in this chapter of our text;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and be cautious about cutting near the nerve and the vein, and make your movements so as to extract the arrow without risk.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	quickly or cautiously, firmly or gently; and guide the patient according to their form before the arrow fell.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For this is the greatest aid one can give, and if you cannot manage it yourself, then follow what the sign shown to you instructs.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another side, or if it reveals any matter of concern, or if the skin is swollen in a spot where you can see or feel it distinctly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut there up, as long as the forceps can take hold, and then grasp: if the arrow jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, twist your hand round as long as she enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull her out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then continue the extraction until it comes out forcefully.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is an arrow in him and he pulls at its shaft, hold onto it throughout its length;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if he has defecated, and you see it being administered with force, then administer one tool for hair removal;
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters into the hair of the tool; and then apply strength.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if the arrow is embedded, then I use one or two pointed instruments to enter it, in order to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is struck, then you should cut all the surrounding flesh or where the wound begins, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then treat the wound as it should be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits or pierces or in the belly or bladder or ribs and is close, then you should cover it up if you can, and if you do;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And beware not to cut the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then suture the wound; this is a skillful task.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And continue with the treatment until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used for extracting arrows resemble a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they are made in sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The form of the root of hair is also like the feathers of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	because of shooting at the tip of the arrow, as this is its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for shooting and retrieving is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	from the veins of common horns
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	From veins from which we cleanse ourselves are thirty-one, of which there is a head of sixteen.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This means:
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	And the two arteries that are in the two temples, visible;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins that are in the sockets of the two eyes, which are called 'aspirers';
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is within the forehead; and the vein that is at the head under the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugulars which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called 'aeugheirich';
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are around the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which we commonly treat are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic vein, and it runs along the left side of the chest, and they call this "the head's vein";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic veins,;
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And they call this "the heart's vein"; and the basilic is either on the right side of the chest or on the left,;
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And they call this medical condition "the wound of the belly", and it is located on the flank,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and that which can be cured, which becomes visibly open on the side.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salve well is the vein located between the thumb and the index finger, and it extends for two inches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the feet are located there are three veins: one is below the knee on the left side of the body,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And it is the second joint, which is at the ankle on the right side; and there is a vein that is called 'Nesse', that is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The health of the veins that are behind the ears helps with the cataracts and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of the healer, as I have told you, and that you find relief in helping yourself.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then pinch the patient's neck at the base of their head.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	Until the two veins can be seen behind the ears in two dependent locations near the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Place your hands thereon, and where you feel the pulse under your hand, if you wish to proceed;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the scalpel and make an incision through the vein as close to the bone, then lift your hand all the way up to the vein above.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	And cut and stretch the skin and the vein well through two inches, and let blood flow out as long as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then hold and bind it until it heals.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of the incision and the cautery or in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The health of the two arteries that are in the temples is akin to an old ailment,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	And indeed, and ointment used for eye care, and in the case of feverish tears from the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And that quality which a physician should be is as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And they pull their throat until the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse all across your chest, and then touch it to see if it beats evenly.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lift the knife above the vein near your thumb tip, and hold the lancet downwards,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein upwards, and press it, just like you did in .ij. other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the needle, place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put cotton over it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and form the wound after that, and let it heal until it is well; and we have spoken about this in relation to its treatment and extraction, or at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The treatment of a vein on the forehead is equally valuable to the treatment of the frontal sinus in old diseases, and for migraines, and for flushes;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is that the illnesses twist their necks by being squeezed, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called a 'digester', whose shape is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another tool, allowing blood to flow out according to the amount you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release the patient's neck, and secure the vein until it is sound and without any trace of the operation.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Always, it is not suitable for the flames to be too intense; and the healing is from side-to-side, because the bone is close, and accidentally breaks the flames when it becomes subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in the two eyelids helps with the eyes, and for the nose, and for the cheek, and around the eye socket in the eye, and for diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their healing is such that the patient tightens its neck by twisting through any kind of connection, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then heal it, and make the healing passage through the skin, slightly longer than the length of the flame somewhat wide, for there is nothing rotten.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by chance should they break; then make correspondence with the blood, as much as you need to, and then bind onto cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The healing of the vein near the nose is valued for fever, and sudden recovery, and diseases of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	likewise for migraines and redness that comes to the face, and likewise when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And the quality of health is such that the sick person narrows their throat, then strains their nose with your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the fine long flame, and place it inside the lip in the space that is between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein doesn't open properly yet, and the blood will now start to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and don't go too deep there, and let the blood flow gently according to your need, then leave it overnight, for she is restored very quickly;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is how it forms with fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The health of the two inguinal glands assists in the tightening of the artery and the beginning of mixture disease, and for many illnesses, and in gangrene, corrosion, and herpes, as well as inflammations;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of health is such that the patient restricts its neck on both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And let the masters be above the head of the patient, and the patients lie on one side for half a bed-length.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then open the vein long enough slightly more than its width, then guide blood moderately, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then make another incision in the other vein, then release the constriction, and press moderately on the veins.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient doesn't suffocate; and leave it until morning, so that the wound heals.
De la sainie des leivres	On the treatment of wounds
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The treatment of veins above the lips helps in closing them in the mouth, and it deals with gum decay, cracks in the lips, nosebleeds, and tooth pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of this treatment is to have the patient stand in front of you, and hold his neck as I have described;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other is on the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And their identification is by their being black, and by the fact that within them there are thin, small veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Thus treat both of them, and if you do not recognize them, be in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	If you take the largest one from each side, and do exactly the same with the two veins above and below, for it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the cure of the throat
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The healing of veins situated near the tongue requires assistance after the healing of the cephalic area, and this is done through constriction of the throat. This also deals with ailments of the eyeball, and diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the qualities of the surgeon are such that the patient's body should be exposed to sunlight while it is in their hands. Then they raise the tongue and look below each side where there may be a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Thus ensuring both sides are healthy, but not too far forward either, because they are close to the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm that we commonly treat are treated according to two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	If they prick at all one large flame brand or an olive stick so fine like a knife blade, and it is called 'anevil'.
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And they are wide yet subtle according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the fire brand Mirtin is greatly renowned, and it is quite wide as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	It is necessary to open the large veins filled with visible abundant blood, and containing much blood and turbidity;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And this is the shape of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it's more subtle and pointed, and it's for purifying the delicate veins, or having subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The purification of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are around the throat, and in the neck, and in the stomach, and in the abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is for the doctor to purify carefully, and to be aware of the artery that is around.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if it severs an artery, and blood begins to flow out, should this occur, you must stop the bleeding, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and it should not be held in the flame, but cut like a young animal would.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open clearly, you should extract it and change to another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	Or if you do not want any bone from him, or you cut through his body with the arm's vein: it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And the application of heat before it, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you know where the pulse is, it should be like this: you must stretch out the arm, touching the spot until you find the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the location for cutting, and then tie the arm down, and apply heat to the vein beforehand.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And beware not to cut into the artery when you see the site inflamed, for that is the artery: listen there instead.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it sticking out as high as a child's urine, and the veins are red and subtle, know that this is a vein from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, place your finger for some time, then stabilize your finger until the vein stops bleeding, as has often happened;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Fix his arm and leave it like this, do not move the patient's limbs; and be careful, do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the vein doesn't stop bleeding and you need to, and the medicine isn't available, if you find an artery that's open, do so because it can help the bleeding stop; and make sure the vein stops.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of walnut shell, cut it, and take one half and bind it well up to the other side;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If there is no bleeding, that's fine; if not, clean it up, as we have said, with powders that stop blood flow;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the bandages should not be too tight for the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's connection.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The healing of the vein in the middle is assisted by measures that help control blood flow from above and below it.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is made up of the basilica and the cephalic part, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is important for the surgeon to be aware of the nerve that runs beneath, and if he does not go too far forward, and should find the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it inflates and damages health, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any of them due to its subtlety, then you should heal the wounded with alcohol beforehand; and listen to the nerve through your skill.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two hands, cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The treatment for a headache, when blood flows from the head, and helps with eye problems;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to use a remedy in the oil flame or in the mint flame, for this is the safest of all veins, because there is neither nerve nor artery nearby.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	In short, it's necessary to choose the lightest weight possible and not to worry if one needs to do it first time, and then repeat;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance swellings occur in some men at their first appearance, but they cause no pain.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you need to know about being a surgeon is that surgery is conducted solely for the purpose of preserving health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid future diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	And let healing take place at one of the three veins that are cut: these are to be known as the scalp vein, the facial vein, and the basilic vein;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And let healing occur at the beginning of prayers while kneeling, and in autumn and after winter following meals, when the signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And let healing begin on the first or third day, after two hours or one and a half days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing for illnesses does not have a determined time, but only when the need is of the day or necessity, at all hours and in all situations;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not good to heal children until they are twelve years old, nor a woman who carries child for less than one quarter of the months until seven weeks.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Neither should they heal the elderly who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wishes to be healed, in whatever manner that may be, it is necessary for him to cleanse the intestines with a gentle cathartic.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If he has kept some bile back, so that the vessels drain the excess putrefactions harmful to the main members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Not even one who is too full of meat, or drunk, shall be cured until they are strong and not anemic.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And when the healer deals with colic pain, vomiting, abdominal distension, frequent urination in women, and labor, work, watching over patients, and bearing, as well as what quickly diminishes the virtue, or by something from the weapon or injury;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then refine the body's fluids, if it is heavy due to food and drinks and medications, if you have the means;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then in or through a bath, if no defense occurs, to refine the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	And heal from the artery near the inner thigh, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and protect yourself that day of work, and of pain, and of excess, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be bound and anointed, and let the ointment be higher than where it is applied, and rub the arm twice or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then stretch half of the bandage upwards, for if it is too tight or too loose, it cannot properly heal the wound;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the area with hands, until the veins swell, and one feels them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then moisten the flame of a small piece of old oil, then place your left finger on that vein under the shoulder a bit where you intend to cauterize;
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	So that the vein does not burn and rupture at being touched.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that behave like strings when they're cauterized, and some have such high winds flowing through them,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	if indeed when placed over the flame, it retreats to the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus one belongs to these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for in this case one should be aware of these matters regarding the surgeons.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it's good; but if not, you can try again near the original spot or suddenly, provided that the limb is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and the patient feels pain, you should leave it alone for one or two days, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	By chance it may bring about the evacuation of pus; do not immerse or bathe, then restart the cleansing if it suits.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the vessel is small, or the artery is too subtle and you doubt whether any blood comes out as much as you see, so pierce that vessel itself straight down to all the flame.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and then press on it a little faster, so that the limb swells; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb swelling, do not restart the cleansing and instead place a little of the olive oil on it; because it alleviates the body from the blood and heals that part where the oil is.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the oil in each healthy part that you heal for stopping the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And similarly apply the mustard and wax when you place it on the head; if the oil is too thick, it will be sparingly applied.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if a large abscess comes about, which often happens, even when it's not healed before because at that time the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	and if you hurry, soak an sponge in hot water and a little salt and place it on the head for one hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it must be that you do this after the release of blood from the vein, and if it stays in place for any days without turning black or green, so long as it doesn't harm it;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see fit, place on anything of Aloes or of Myrrh dissolved into a Calamus juice, a signifier, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Many times an abscess and its appearance were seen at the healing of the basilica: therefore place your hand there, and if you find the area soft upon pressing with your hand, then it is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not apply anything from what we have said, for by chance it might cut into the artery; but make one plastered bandage to stiffen the area, then treat with another remedy until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each person with blood according to the amount of their virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	But if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see that it's large, let it flow until it becomes thin. And if it's too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for the one who is full and empty, needing blood extraction, you should make him have a larger incision, and let the flames be wide;

Des sainies de ventouse	Cures using suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blasping devices are made from horns, or spiders, or snakes; and bloodletting is performed in two ways: either by piercing to draw blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this kind of bloodletting which involves piercing is done in two ways: either immediately hot (with the wound still bleeding freely), or without heat.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	Bloodletting performed by piercing and extracting blood is carried out during the first twelve days of menstruation,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	One is totally at the head level; and the other is in or near the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And two others on two sides of the neck; and the suction cup under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the suction cup on both shoulders; and the suction cup above the elbows;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the suction cups on both arms; and the suction cups on both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the suction cup on both ankles; and the bloodletting does not aim for blood, but rather for small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And because of this, one does not weaken oneself, as one does in surgery to veins;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered, nor with any fire or sense of heat, in any illness that comes from congestion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of diseases we must use suction, or due to habits, then we administer it each hour at the beginning of her period, or at the end, and throughout and in every time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are those who, when they need to use suction, become pregnant first.

Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the suction cup is as follows: you should apply it first while empty and keep it suctions consistently, applying it quickly, moving it evenly, without stopping this action until you see the skin turning red and inflamed. Then remove it, and replace the suction cups, taking care to notice the body's position because there are some with thick flesh and clear pores: it is proper to pierce once only in each area, and create large wounds, a little deeper; and suck gently.
