Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has two inches and half the length of a palm on each side, and at its center there is an incision that resembles one quarter of an inch, as to pierce a needle in such manner,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And if it's from an animal, let it boil so that it doesn't hurt the patient when applying it to the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And have in the middle a rod across of an earthworm or iron, for putting a candle in possession.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And let them be both large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the suction cups for children are different from those of the elderly, and those for thin people are different from those for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And thus one must put this suction cup onto the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take the wax candle or one line of it, and place it inside the suction cup through the penis which is inside the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the heat remains at the bottom of the suction cup rather than burning the skin;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and you should do so at the location that we have mentioned, so that when needed, if the steam goes up, remove the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And trace the incision like before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup treatment for pleurisy disease, during all stages of illness, there should be neither a lack nor an excess, and it is administered only when it is filled with water, and placed on the body solely.
et c’est li forme:	And this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Thrushes are not treated with suction cups in limbs where it's impossible to place suction cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And on their naked skin from burns, like those of a bull or calf, and others similar;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And this is about water baths: when you find veins that are clean in calm water without infection, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in warm water until they become accustomed and have nothing in their abdomens.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then cleanse the wound and use suction cups, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place the veins on it;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full, and itch, if it is possible to apply a suction cup, then do so, for this works very well.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the arm with ease and water, quite well, and then incision;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the arm is raised too soon after the course of the veins, cool it down with one and a half draps of linen in cold water, and place them on it, until the vein turns red;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if there are multiple veins, place on it powdered vitriol or gall and similar substances until the vein turns red;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	You place half of peeled beans inside the body, and leave them until they dry in the body, then it will now stop bleeding.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more work, take others without fail.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the veins do not want to be taken again, rub with fresh blood or you put a needle inside until blood comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	Then place them and soon as they feel the blood, let them dry;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are bleeding, apply a mixture of aloes and flour or sifted ash to the wound; it will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book on fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the restoration and healing of fractures.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear child, that the leaves of this chapter are filled with matters not found in any of the old books, nor did they ever read a letter from them;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And because of this reason, the knowledge has been withdrawn from our land, for I have never found any good in it;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it, for through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have dealt with the knowledge there, and through experimentation, and by habit from my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described in this chapter what is contained, and summarized it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the previous two chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary for us to outline the essence of this book in its introduction and prologue, and highlight the chapters where wise minds apply their intellect. We should adhere to truth, so that those who have been taught can understand and learn this noble art, and teach it to others as well.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fractures or dislocations or twists occur in any part of the body, if it is necessary to quickly heal the patient on both sides and parts, without anything obstructing your path, like weakness from illness, or children, or elderly people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	Or if the treatment is too vigorous or too cold; and make fresh hot jugs, that means hot baths, and fat ointments and goat cheese, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty foods. And do not fill up with meat that fills the blood veins until you have doubt of a warm abscess or spreading material in the limb. If the patient responds well to their initial treatment as they used it before.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that cause heavy digestion or are viscous, such as cooked wheat in water, and onions, and leeks, and peas, and cow liver, and eggs, and fresh fish, and heavy wine, and similar items.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at any time of loosening they are moved more quickly and quicker is the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones broken in old and weak people do not heal or join well according to their nature due to the withering of limbs, nor also those that are too soft, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but rather apply a cure by fixing the broken bone to its original position, that is through the use of large splints which allow the limb to be joined together, just as it was before; and do not rush its work, for in this situation nourish with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the breakage of the head is different from the breakage of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you all manners of breaking in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that go to the elbow, and others through prodding, such as the size of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it's a broken bone with an injury, or a break resulting in a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each way has its own tool and proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory brings to mind;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	It is known as the breaking of the bone by those whose legs are twisted, and opens well outward, and its pain feels upon pressing with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting or sensitivity in the joints, and patients do not feel much pain, if there's no breaking of bones;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it can well have twisting, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it doesn't suit you to move it with your hand, but apply the remedies that follow, and then gently strain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breaking that occurred in the arm, and which are the two parts separated, now they should be placed level with each other, so that abscesses reach to the veins;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the pus is thick and comes out, if he leaves no day, until the abscess subsides;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it level with the movement you can do gently and wisely, know that restoring it is easier than in those where there are fragments. Then tighten it, as you will see later on this procedure.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is divided into two parts, whether they are hands or feet, or by your hand if it's a small limb, or at two strings, or at one string and by your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and position the limb according to its natural shape, so when the parts of the injured member are relieved, you realign them through all your efforts by moving them as far as you can, and ensure that in your work, no harm or pain befalls the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and properly adjust both ends of the bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with your hand if you think it's not quite right: if it feels good to the touch, and don't strain it too much, don't press like those who bring about abscess drainage and muscle tension in the body as we have many times wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limbs are in place, restrain the patient well so they don't move them, whether awake or asleep, while turning or in any other manner.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And ensure that the limb is so secure that no pain is felt.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when no pain is felt, it is not properly placed, and you should put it in a suitable position so that no pain is felt;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and see to it that it be set straightly, lest any twist or curve remain when it has been restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the quality of the member broken will be according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that limbs broken vary in size and extent, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are smaller limbs, such as arms and legs and alike; it is necessary to envelop them with soft and subtle linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And for those that are larger, such as buttocks and thighs: it is necessary to envelop them with a wide and hard bandage, because the wide bands wrap around the entire large limb, and restrict it equally from all sides, so there is no twist;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then place light bandages around it, three or four times or two depending on the member, and press your hand a little throughout the bandage, then go above the breakage and restrict less, so that the breakage can move slightly away from the breakage;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften that ligament a little bit by a little bit, until you grasp a large part of the healthy side, then take another ligament, and return back and forth on the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then go to the part near the breakage, and gently tighten it, neither too hard nor too soft, as we have said in our first instruction above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the heated linen or cloths, until it is perfectly even, then tie everything with one bandage and afterwards put your well made pins on top, if there's no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something soothing over it, that removes the swelling, and leaves it like this for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then hold onto your stars, and let them be half the width of a standard reed, or made from the shafts used for making sticks, or from the stems of palm trees, and shape them like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the stars placed on the break be a little bigger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and let them be as long as is needed for limbs of smallness or greatness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold them on the stars in the same way you did at the first trial, then tie above it an addition string, just like at the first trial on the breakage;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	The more narrow it is hereafter, sooner; hence one should have a thread medium in size, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the thread is thick, as with works that bind linens to wooden frames with twisted linen cords, and this is a great mistake, because the binding cannot be uniform if it is too fine, and it does not suit for there to be less than half a do of space between each nail.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patients are sore from the nails of the stakes after the tightening at their healthy parts, then put patches of linen or shoddy wool on them, so they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is inflamed and the joints are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not right to constrain all limbs broken on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not recommended to bind them with splints for more than 5 days or 7, or longer depending on the duration of each healing process occurring.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method of the old plastering to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that stands on the walls of a mill, mix it with plenty of eggs, and prepare this concoction not too dry nor too thick, and use it, which is the common way of applying restoring plaster in various configurations, and equally for women and small children, as neither is too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method for the plastering that restores fractures and dislocations: take three parts of saffron, nine parts of cardamom, eight parts of rue, and one part of asafetida and gum Arabic, in a ratio of .x.3; add myrrh and aloes in the amount of .v.3; mix seven parts of vinegar with this concoction; if the mixture is warm, use this plaster, for it has good composition and heals broken bones quickly, and is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method for plastering in case of twisting: take mugwort and valerian, each 3 grams; myrrh and aloes, each 8 grams; acacia, 6 grams; boric acid from Armenia, 10 grams, grind well, mix with water or enough egg white, then apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method for dressing fractures and removing bone pieces, easing pain arising therefrom, and the use of bone cutting and bruising: take new wool, and cook its grease in oil, then place it on the affected area. These dressings do not heal completely but are better for soothing abscesses and properly treating bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method for dressing broken bones that heals them: take dried fig leaves and land beech leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method for plastering during the restoration of bone fracture and to promote the healing of the abscess. Take root of vervain, chamomile, flowers of violettes, flour of borage, from each one part; and grind it all together, mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix with wet coriander water or just plain water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method for plastering more forcefully than the first one when an abscess is being restored in a limb. Take roots of vervain and flaxseed, balm, melilot, and wormwood, and flowers of violet and chamomile, from each take one part; grind it all together, mix with salt water or sweet water, or with wine depending on the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates states that to restore strength in a fractured limb one should apply a salve made of beeswax and oil, and nothing else more. He says it should be between two layers neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that we should place upon the broken limb for restoration, things slightly moistened but somewhat warm, such as mirr (mastic), aloe, incense and similar things, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method for dressing injuries and pain: take the fat and feathers from cooked sheep or goose carcasses, or bird feathers, and ground coriander seeds equally with them. Grind all these ingredients together to create a poultice which you apply to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Then after a short while, be sure that the patient does not feel any pain and that there is no movement in their bone at its location. If it was not dislocated by hand movements.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain starts at the site, or itching appears, if there's no rest or swelling, then you must act quickly, and reposition it, then apply the poultice; take a light cloth and a wet sponge from the sea, immerse them in water, and hold over his head until the itching stops and the pain is alleviated.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then allow the limb to rest for an hour, then place it on dry wool, moistened with water or rose oil, and tie it up with a bandage until you are sure of removing any pus.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And allow the inflammation to settle on the limb, and alleviate the pain, then resume the gentle treatment, a bit of plaster, and do not exert force as before; continue with subtlety until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you notice that pus and redness, pain and swelling are subsiding, indicating the injury has healed throughout, then you need plaster and bandaging; start again as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have discussed happens to the limb, or it does not relax until after three days, four days, five days, seven days; and each time let it rest for twenty days according to observation, as long as the healing process continues, approaching the realignment of the bone.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore, maintain the restraint longer than before, and let his meat grow bigger, as I said earlier. And if you see that his body dries out more than it should, know that no remedies can come from this situation;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Let the hot water cure him whenever you reset his shoulder, and do this every third day, and gently clean a bit of the wound;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this work, cut out the dislocations from the limb, and hasten what foolish remedies cause, that deform the limb brutally: this is bad, and such operations are useless, and I see no other solution than to leave it alone and operate properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Through various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of breaks exist, and various shapes, and their causes are designated;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are breaks caused by the impact of a sword, and injuries to the neck that involve breaking all the bone up to the joint socket at the base of the skull, as with an axe or cudgel; because of this, such types of breakage are called "axehurts".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or when the sword penetrates the bone from above without passing through, this type of breakage is called "absolute"; and both large and small wounds result from these two kinds of breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or crack in the bone, or injury from stone, or impact on stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break that approaches until it reaches the tissue beneath the bone, or above the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound penetrating the bone as thin as a hair, and this crack is small, and due to this it is called that "hairline" fracture;
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made either by hitting with a stone or falling or any similar thing that causes the bone fragment to go inward, and makes the limb bend as blacksmiths do when they are working on pots; it enters the stone inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more in those who have wet bones below such as in an adult's thigh bone;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And occurs through all these ways of breaking where small fragments are lost as with these; and I will discuss them in their own right.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of breakages through the diminishment above them, and the examination at stakes, and by the corrupt flesh which is upon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair can be recognized when one has exposed the bone and rubs it inside, revealing the black breakage.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating breakage, beware of adverse effects due to malaise, and if you do not encounter any bad side effects such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, stretching, pallor, fever ague, and other symptoms appearing in various conditions, it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming mishap, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when winter comes first to you, and if it is winter, then it's necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is spring, then you should hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, in such a way that the pus around the bone is rotten, and accidents occur as we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone break reaches up to the membrane covering the brain, it is necessary that you split the broken part like this: and when you take hold of the head from the affected side, and expose on the bone in all manners that you can, and more according to the appearance of the wound as much as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if the flow of blood comes to reveal the bone, or when an abscess ruptures, you use what is necessary, and it is that you fill the wound with wet bandages soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And let the wound rest until the abscess is calmed and there's no more pain from bleeding; then begin working towards the bone to remove it. This task can be done in two ways as described in this chapter: one way is that you cut precisely at the front, which forms:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various sizes of knives, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of hard iron; and you use them lightly in your work so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is too hard, you should drill it internally, so as to apply cuts with awls without going through the soft tissue beyond the bone, and there must be a margin or a circle of about one inch above the point that does not allow the point to go beyond the bone; and you need more than one, so that each goes into its place of the thickness of the bone, so that you have awls for all sides; and this is the shape of the three types of awl cuts.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for drilling through the bone is to place an awl on the bone and twist with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced. Then remove the awl a little further, and do this all around, then cut out the space between the fractures of the bone, and do it as finely and gently as possible, while still using light force, as we have said, either by hand or any tool you have such as tweezers; make sure not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is fitting that you retain the preparation left from the bone to all half inches. However, it must be sturdier and more delicate than another incisor;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if there remains no little bones or any scales, then gently remove them with tools of a half-inch size; then treat the wound with the gauze and remedies that we have discussed.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of treatment is this, as Galien stated, which is more sparing; and it uses a strong knife, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover a part of the bone where the fracture opens and moves. So when you have uncovered that part, place underneath the tip of this ophthalmic incisor, as described here:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side alone, and have the part divided into two ribs, so that when you are cutting it faces the bone; then with a small hammer from above, so you strike lightly across the entire bone, and be well cautious of the cloth which is nearby;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it pushes against the bone, do so lightly, because you can feel the bone cause harm and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not pierce until the cloth and only cuts through from above, with small pieces remaining, then after that roughness, use a fine razor to remove the scales. You must have various quantities of this tool in order to administer the most suitable treatment for each location according to the manual and the appearance of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you stand before great razors, and after finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other hair cutting and delicate breakage, you must adjust your actions according to their direction; this is something that cannot be done by someone who has devoted their study to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if it is exposed during surgery, it should be that you take .1 drachm of linen, according to the size of the wound, and mix it with rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another piece of cloth, doubled either two or three times, and soak it in wine and rose oil, then place it on the first layer; do this as lightly as you can, without burdening the syfac, then apply a layer of lint over it, but don't pull it tightly enough that it only touches the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And let them be like that for one or two days, until the abscesses have subsided, then release them and apply medicine if it is roots of basil, flour of yew, incense powder, and arisole, and similar things; and make a powder from these things, place it on the wound, and administer antiseptic medicines immediately without causing any irritation.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And see to it that the wound is cleaned immediately, do not leave any ointment behind, nor allow it to assemble in the brain fabric. For when something assembles over the web of the mind, it causes harm and leads to great distress; because when you place a biting thing on the head, it gets irritated from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, so that no harmful events occur to the patient as we have said, in case there is doubt without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if death does not come from what medicine we have placed upon it, assuming this has the necessary effect, then you should take one part of honey, and three parts of rosegum oil and one drachm of glue, and place this mixture on the face;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then continue with treatments as needed until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two parts above the nose are broken, or only one if necessary, as these consist of two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, it does not break, nor will it allow bending or twisting once healed.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should press your little finger or tip under the nose and make an equal break inside to your second finger, and at the nostril opening outwardly, until the nose revives according to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is above the nose part and cannot reach to its place at the head, then it is necessary that you make it equal to the tip of a stick somewhat thick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, then remake the treatment, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	But if not, after the seventh or eighth day when the abscess has calmed down, then apply a poultice of linen to the nose tip, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you pull one to another on the other side, if breaking occurs; and make sure they are as large as they fill the cavities in the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they say that one should moisten the tents with butter and change each day. I don't think it's correct, but rather they should be moistened in the preparation of egg yolk mixed with powder from grinding; then let the tent remain until the bone is hard and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And every time you pull out the original or nose feathers in place of the tents, and if it's one egg with an inner layer of skin, and keeps the wound intact, and lets the air pass through; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose in the same way as you are doing it, then put a poultice or wet cotton in oil mixed with it, or in one corner of a spoonful of snail juice.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if abscesses do not come out, you should apply plaster to the surface, made of ash powder and incense powder. Mix it with yolk oil, then place light wadding on top and don't bind it too tightly;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the bone fracture is small and broken into many pieces, when you can use suitable tools for this task, then cut along the crack, and clean out the fragments of soft tissue, and stitch them together, as with plasters and ointments that are suitable for this purpose;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound within the bone, then you can clean it out and put on cloths soaked in vinegar, as long as it is sound.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken externally, and there's no wound outwardly, only the fracture is external. It isn't broken into two halves completely; rather it breaks internally as well, which can be discerned lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, should the break occur in the right part of the jawbone, to press your index finger into the mouth at the site where the patient is suffering; and if the break occurs in the left mandibular part, you must use your index finger from the right hand, press gently on the break internally, and then proceed with the operation by making an incision externally with the other hand.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if there is a break in both parts of the jawbone, it must be treated with extension of half parts, until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if tooth movements occur, or rupture, then hold them with a thread of gold, silver or silk. Then place wax on the broken jaw, and place two pieces of cloth on top; and place one large pad well made under this cloth piece, or a leather piece equal to it in length and width according to the jaw size, and tie it on as much as you can. Command the patient to rest, and have light meals.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, then reposition it on the third day and thereafter put back into place whatever has shifted; apply plaster to this area, mix powdered chalk with abundant egg or sesame flour after removing the wax; cover the plaster with fine wool, and when the plaster hardens and the patient's position does not change anymore, let them be like that until they are healed; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if pus-filled ulcers come about, then apply what we have repeatedly instructed.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture combined with a wound together, reward nothing of the bone has been removed; so much skill in extracting tools needed for this task is required.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is nothing left, if the wound is wide, place one plaster over it suitable for this purpose to promote healing until it heals.
de la forcele	with strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks many times before reaching the shoulder, and each break occurs in three ways: it may break completely and be separated into two parts, leaving fragments that are easier to restore; or there might be a break accompanied by an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And in the cases where there is a break accompanied by an injury, if you have two helpers, so that one marks the shoulder where the force breaks; and the other extends their hand towards the affected part. Then align the break with your fingers, ensuring the shape matches how it should be, without any appearance or movement of the break.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round sponge of cloth or wool under the shoulder and side, with its size according to your needs; stretch out and lift the force (meaning pressure), while restraining the sponge in your hand so that you can align the break correctly, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head from the strength's force behind it, because it comes forward, then the patient must lie with their head resting on their pillow, and place one of the shoulder's cushions under both shoulders. Have the attendants press the shoulder downwards until the bone of the strength rises.

et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and make it resemble a spoon, and do not use it in the wrong place, and be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the scale of the work; and have two holes, as you see fit, and one should be wide and the other narrow, as they are the lines of the wound that you made when treating the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are assured of the removal of the abscess, if you suture the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt about the removal of the abscess, if you cover the wound with bandages and tents according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And when the abscesses are drained, if it is moist, soak bandages in oil rose and in sweat and wine, and place them on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The abrasion of the bone, when it is affected by wounds and surgery, involves placing on the bone a plaster made from grinding powder and yolk of egg, and you place light bandages on top. puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very large bandage about the size of your palm in width, then place two double bandages on top of the bandages and plaster. et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And place the instrument on the wound, and turn the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the diseased one; and manipulate each part separately. de la brisure de l’espaule	From the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Sometimes the shoulder breaks or splits at its end or in the middle, and it might be dislocated by just touching it; if you handle it according to the shape of the break and reset it following its natural form, in all possible ways. de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it breaks more often at the end. And when it's broken in the middle, it gets tilted downwards, causing great pain for the patient, lack of control, and they might suddenly vomit blood, and the movement opens up within the broken bone, and one can clearly feel this sensation.

And in the restoration process, if the patient has been laid on their back, and you place them one and a half cubits between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and unite both ribs with your hands. de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Regarding the breaking of the shoulder.

The other method is that you fix the skin on his neck, and tie the hand to the neck, then command two attendants that one of them shaves the one above the wound with their hands, and the other cuts down to all half an inch, and extend each in their respective parts.

Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And when you see the position of the stakes and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, if you doubt about removing an abscess, if you let it bind until the seventh day, as we have said; then watch each three days the binding, so that itching does not swell up or come to the site where there should not be any pus coming out because it is too tight. If it heals, as we have said.

And if no such events occur, or if the dislocation takes two days or more after the start of the healing process, and if the patient remains comfortable on his back with his hands on his stomach; place one inch thick wool under the shoulder for each hour during which he is to rest. The medicine heals it by its virtue and provides the meat we have placed before as treatment, ensuring that the meat is thoroughly absorbed; when he starts to recover, if it's large. It's customary for both the shoulder and leg to be healed within forty days after all procedures; then you must dislocate again and administer baths and medicines for local treatments until complete recovery.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the 'fosciles'. One bone is smaller, and it is this one that protects the elbow; while the other bone is larger, and it is this one that lies beneath the small head. Sometimes only the large foscile breaks or both might break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the smaller fosciles break, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the larger ones break, the healing is poorly done, and more painful than when they broke together. If it's only the small foscile that breaks, then gently extending it slightly, and putting it on equal footing would be sufficient.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the larger foscile that breaks, then you should pull more tightly; and extend it on a cushion, and elevate the elbow of your hand higher than the others, and the smaller fingers lower than the other fingers, and have the patient cross their fingers over themselves, and another cushion in front of them raised, so high that the hand does not suffer any strain; then extend your servant's arm to the part above his hand, or at the elbow, and one other assistant on the other side. Then place the mirror evenly according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if during the breaking into pieces, you place each back in its original position, and if none of them is broken to be grasped by the hand, and you cannot restore it to its original position, then you do work on and the bone, as we said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if during the wound caused by the breakage, which I have discussed in the single chapter; take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if during the beginning of the restoration there are abscesses present, then apply .i. a strip of cerate made from rosin and white beeswax, ensuring it is neither too hard nor too soft; and bind this strip finely above so that when the abscesses are alleviated, they are soothed. Then remove the cerate, and replace with plaster made by mixing the powder from the mill with plenty of egg whites; place the splints hereafter, making sure that the splint corresponding to the breakage is more prominent, slightly wider than the others. And you should know that there must be seven or eight splints in various positions: whether the breakage affects one bone, two bones, and it binds more above the breakage than elsewhere, as I have explained at the beginning of this chapter; and ensure the strips covering the breakage are soft and moist, neither hard nor rough; and use threads made from linen that are not too thick or too thin, as we said. And keep up to bind the limb and its joints for several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad occurrences come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it should be that you warm the limb with hot water, until that itch is calmed; and let the limb not be left to rest. And then restart constriction, and when this ligament has been split and these bones have been exposed, and similar things, if they are treated properly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if precaution is taken so that no distresses cannot come to the limb because it is too constricted, it should be that you soften it with pox (a kind of compress or poultice), and leave it in this manner for a few days, until the distresses have passed, and then you should tighten.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things that we have spoken about come to the patient, or if it is allowed to remain unrelieved for up to 20 days. Or until then, then place their hands on the neck and make sure the necks are even, and take care not to move them or to dislocate anything, and let them rest on their back; and know that this swelling has been restored in about 30 days or about 45 days, and perhaps around 20 days depending on the compositions and the nature of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and around our thumbs there are few breaks, and only bending happens many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the sole of the hand is broken or bent, it should be treated so that the parts heal in a straight line and directly in front of him equally; then place his hand on an extended surface, and extend the fingers with the broken bones, placing them evenly under each eye, until they are properly aligned; then apply the bandage and splints if no abscess forms, and then place an elevation according to the size of his bed; and wrap it in one layer of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is in the heel near the belly of the sole, make a cone of linen and instruct the patient to place it on his broken foot; then draw it tightly onto the heel, and ensure that the elevation is as wide as the hand's sole, and adjust so it fits properly.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the breakage is at the front, it is necessary to place an electrode above and another under in the sole of the foot, so that the hand be open and straight, then tie it completely around the hand, and seal the connection between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the breakage affects neither of my fingers, it's the thumb case, and you should place them equally, as is appropriate; and apply pressure with the sole, and if you see fit to use a small right electrode to lift the breakage, and keep it still; and if the breakage occurs on one of the other fingers like in the index or any other, then you should place them equally, and tie them with a healthy finger that follows; or you can tie all together, considering each's position, or you put an electrode here like you would for the thumb; take care in maintaining and arranging the treatment at each stage, and help those who are coming up against problems, as I have explained.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken kneecap
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the elbow is often broken, and one can see it when it turns in front and behind; and the restoration happens as follows: first, one ties a bandage above the break, and secondly underneath it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the wounds lie on their face, then stretch each of their joints to their equal parts; and this is when the break has reached into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And when the break is close to the elbow joint's base, then tie one ligament towards the wrist, and the other ligament below the break. Similarly, if it is close to the knee, in which case place one ligament behind the knee, and the extension downwards; then place the bones equal to their two hands until they follow its natural figure, and then apply plaster and bandage, and should no abscess occur.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess to deal with, let it heal first before returning to your work and treatment; the incision is made in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the wound. i.e., bandage it tightly in two or three layers, and retain the excess, then bend the leg until the heels reach the root of the thigh, and insert one long thread between the calf and the leg, under the knee, and guide the thread up through the loops; then continue to wrap around the leg and calf with the bandage, then place a wick on top of the wound, and place another wick on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and calf with strips of cloth so as to make the pressure equal, then begin to bind tightly in three or four turns around the wound; and when you go beyond the wound, bind more loosely; then take two threads that you have inserted between the leg and calf, and bind them with three wicks placed above, then return under the thread where it was coming from until you reach the ankle; and tighten, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, then if there is no abscess, swelling or other symptom.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens that it dislocates again, reposition as what we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that catch, it is necessary to extract them if possible; and if you cannot, then it is necessary to cut through the wound, and drain the fluid; and treat in the way we have said, until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the skin broken in such a way when these needles are inserted, as in the shoulder and arm; however, during this kind of treatment, there should be no harm to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the skin is restored in about one day, or somewhat more or less depending on individual differences.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the garden alley
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the garden alley there is little breakage, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it's usually just a crack, or two pieces missing, and appears on any wound, and even without a wound, and one feels this well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.
