de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg are two bones, of which one is called by its right name "tibia" and the other is called "fibula"; and any injury or breakage occurs similarly as with the arm, and for this reason, the restoration method is exactly like that for the arm, and the procedures are all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if two bones are broken together, then turn the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then turn in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the larger bones are broken, then one feels great pain and sees it clearly; turn away from there. Then apply extension, make it equal, and fasten the ligaments equally; but still, when the break is ugly and consists of many pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have accomplished your task, take two ropes of hawser that bind the leg on both sides and are as long as the leg from the knee down to there; then wrap them twice around each of the two large ligaments above and below, tying them in the middle so that the leg cannot move either right or left. And thus it is well done; and no one should treat with a single rope of this length made of hawser, and they put the leg to rest from movement, doing this properly at the break where there is an injury; and move the leg every day to see if any abscess forms or any other incident occurs; heal it as long as it is sound.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From the breaking of bones at the knee
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle it does not come from breaking, but with bones at the knee breaking occurs and in the legs, there is only force that acts in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if breaking occurs at the bones of the knee, and you see these bones press one against another, place those bones in the ground like they wanted to go, just as it would with them trying to move. Then place your foot on their spot where the bones are lifted, press it there until they regain movement in their joints; then apply plaster and bandages over it, and place a small table under his knee for about two inches, then force the knee to its normal position, then wrap cloths around it and other things you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And once three or four days have passed, you'll find that the ligaments are equal; whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the ribs are broken, restore them as we have said about the ribs of the hand. Then place a piece under each broken rib according to its length, slightly longer than the rib itself, then place that base on the table I mentioned, and hold it in position; and if there are two or three or more broken ribs, break them, and then for each rib put a piece according to its quantity, wrapped in one piece of linen, and hold the table under this; and while standing over the front edge of the table facing the belly of the wound, make sure to secure it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other injuries, once we've discussed them; and attend to each incident according to how it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the hand bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the natural womb is broken, if she lets it swell, then incline her to the lower part of the back, and hold her from behind; then fill the opening of nature with cotton, and put in such an amount as half a stick; then make the woman stand up again slowly and gently lift her back bit by bit, and then let the cotton spring out until it reaches the entrance of nature, bringing the bone along with the stick; and when she wishes to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has done so, put it back in place, repeating this process for seven days or more: if you see that healing is occurring, take a goat bladder, tie a piece of cane to its opening, and fill the whole bladder with nature; then blow into the cane forcefully until the bladder inflates internally. The natural process will correct the breakage; afterward, fill it with cotton and let her rest for some more days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the hand is broken or that of someone else, if it can be restored as we have said concerning the thigh bone; and do not ignore these injuries for those who devote their efforts to them, and hear my book. For the breakage signifies in various positions the right way of restoration: hence, understand this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of a broken penis, take an oyster shell and fill it with the penis; then wrap it securely in cloth, and leave it for three days or as long as needed, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it's large, like in the case of a rib or shoulder blade or similar, that it be treated surgically now, so that the surgeries we have mentioned can attest to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healing well, one may use vinegar to do so, should you have nothing else; then proceed to heal the fracture in that same hour or day. If abscesses form and remain there, however, then start again on the treatment of the fracture at that point.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And should abscesses continue to form and remain there, let the healing process continue for a new day, until the abscesses are subdued. Don't touch them on the third or fourth day, as you would cause unwanted complications.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken and visible under the uncovered part of your body, you should place it lightly with your hands, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear for you to place it evenly with your hands, then take this tool made of iron which is .vij. or .viij. inches long, and its width corresponds to the size of the wound; and in each case of a broken bone, the surgeon must insert three or four (depending on his needs), according to what he requires for each treatment of fracture; it should be round and slightly thick so that it does not bend under compression against your limb when working, and it should be sharp at both ends, and thick at the middle towards the front.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called 'palainche', so that the curved ends of the bone should be placed on the tip of the visible bone; and strike once, as long as it holds, and make them even against each other. And if the breakage is subtle, and the tools are unable to properly grasp the bone, then you must hold onto the tip of the bone until the tools have the ability to do so.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, if you have a suitable tool for this purpose, such as an incisor or awl, use your strength; then remove what is left in the bone of roughness and small flakes.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone has been returned and the patient feels intense pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. Do what you can to have it back there, then apply one part of vinegar tincture mixed with black wine; and if this happens in a dry state; and do not put anything like plaster or other thing on the wound where there was an open sore, so that no gangrene or corruption comes about; then give these remedies after you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and apply the dressing all over according to the size of the wound, and take care well that the wound not be strained with friction; and many times have people done this wrongly, causing harm or decay to the patient; and let your treatments be softer and less aggressive than other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is deep or large and you doubt that harmful occurrences might happen there, as we have said earlier, and you find pain in the area, then it does not suit to apply remedies; but cover everything neatly instead of applying remedies, with tough bandages and secure them. And when after one or two days you see improvement on the wound bed, so remove what you had put against all wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrarmocon's ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it must be that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it is joined and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it should be that the limb is placed so that the bone goes back up slightly gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if this continues for several days, and it can't join at all back to its place, know that there are small pieces of bone, so you should treat the wound with a plaster bandage, and remove all these pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if it leads to a fistula in the place or any other form of corruption, then you should treat it according to what he explained in his chapter above. And when the bone is broken and exposed at the limb, such as the bones of the elbow or shoulder joint, or others like large limbs, do not treat it; many times this leads to death, but let it heal naturally; by chance, it might close after about 20 days or 30 days. Then if you can, cure the wound; if not, leave it as is.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The burns that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see burns after rubbing the skin by the breeze, especially near joints. An ugly thing to see is how the member's figure becomes; and by chance cannot perform its natural actions on the body.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take caution then when it is fresh: if you administer any stictch medicines such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, sarsagall, aniseed, and similar others, do so according to your preference for any of these things or all together, and mix them with a stichtic wine or with plenty of egg or with vinegar; then apply it on the skin in poultices, squeeze well, and do not remove by hand; afterwards remove it, and start another application until all the lumps are removed. Or you apply on a well-made piece of plaster; for the properties of the plaster so are that it removes all swellings above the limbs; and if the lump has turned into hardness like stone and needs to be removed, then cover it from below, and let the excess show clearly; or take it away with any knife until it is completely removed, and continue treating until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the member which becomes weak after garrisoning
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone has been restored and afterwards, the limbs are weak and subtle, this happens due to various reasons: because it was tied too tightly and not as it should be; or because there were too many bindings, and no relief could come to the limb; or due to an excessive amount of swelling; or due to large movements that did not occur in their time; or because he has little blood in his body, being weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you must eat the disease for him, and make his body soft, until the abscess multiplies within him; then give him baths, and make him happy and relaxed. Then put ointment on the limb, so that the ointment attracts to the large swelling, and washes it with cold water frequently, until the swelling aligns with the limb; and restore its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If the member is bent after illness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and if the bones were broken apart during this process, even though the shape of the limb becomes ugly afterward; yet it does not lose its natural function. Do not believe in those who say one must break the limb anew entirely; many people have followed this advice in our land; these procedures are criticized and lead to great harms and even death. Nonetheless, if the swellings and pains from the injury are still fresh, they should be treated with hot water applications or with boiled soothing herbs like leaves of fennel, roots, and melilot, among other such remedies. And apply one part of a moisturizing plaster; take figs in oil, grind them with cumin seeds, and similar medicinal substances that soften the wound. Prepare this with oil from sesame or grease, then apply as a plaster on top; alternatively, you can gather fatty figs, crush them together with flour from cumin, and other such medicines that reduce inflammation, mix it with fat from lard or oil from safflower, and apply it as a plaster.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And whenever there is an injury to the joint, continuously rub it with wet hands for a long time. And each hour apply movement to the affected limb.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twists are aged and hardened, like bone, and it requires being treated with fire, then cover up to the bone, incising subtly lightly; and apply consideration and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the patient.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation affects any part, if the situation requires it now, you should attempt to reduce or reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays and the joints swell, and by chance resets it to its original position; because it is not good to move it when it's swollen at that location: many times this brings pus and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	If this happens, when you encounter such a situation, have the surgeon attend to the patient, and let them rest until all the pus has subsided; then immerse the limb in hot water and oil, gently move it afterwards, and treat each part according to its natural position.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on shoulder dislocations up until this point.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated downwards, and the dislocations of both jaws occur in two ways: either they are somewhat bone-like at their roots and somewhat softened; or they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the bottom, and expel saliva from the mouth so that they cannot hold it, nor can they close their mouths, and wrap their tongue with their speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can return through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it's complete and accomplished, you should reset it quickly without hesitation;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the doctors cut into the head of the patient, and insert their fingers from one of their hands into the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is 2 inches; and the other hand should be out of the mouth to keep it level. And instruct the patient to soften, their jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And keep the fingers steady until they return to their place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if bringing it back causes pain, similarly when the two jaws are together, if they come from hot water and oil, as long as you gently bring them back; do not burn during the attempt to return them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient feels well when softened, if you place wet cloths in the form of a poultice made from rose oil and beeswax, then bind it gently with soft strings.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient rest on their back, and if their shoulders are placed between two cushions, so they do not move to either side or strain themselves, but feed them light food until the pains have subsided, and secure the jaws.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then test this to see if it can be slightly lifted, and does not struggle with opening the mouth for eating or drinking, until the lower jaw is well healed and sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two lower jaws cannot be properly aligned within an hour and are not turned back to their original position, fever and chronic fatigue will result, and in some cases, abdominal pain or vomiting will occur.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times, death befalls the one who undergoes this within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the lever (referring to mechanics or possibly medical tools)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forces cannot displace from within along the middle of the chest and the back; it is displaced only outward, and one feels this clearly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is such that when you lie back on your back and stretch your arms out; then press with your hands to form them like a palm, she will return; then place on the plaster and the bandage, and compress her.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the head that is towards the knife cannot be set back; if it's not able to return like this, and when it does get displaced once, you should reset it to its place as we have said; then place on the plaster and the bandage, compress her, and instruct the patient to rest until she becomes well.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And similarly, the head of the shoulder is brought back when it's set free from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	On the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one way is when it dislocates at the part below the clavicle and above the elbow; and the second way is at the part near the heel; and sometimes dislocates at the part above, which happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And the shoulder does not dislocate behind or inside the nerves; and many times it dislocates downward towards the elbow, even in those with little flesh, because in these cases it moves quickly; for those with enough flesh, it jumps to points, and returns to its place.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	By chance, it happens to some men from a blow or dislocation, and the shoulder swells with an abscess filled with heat, and they think that she is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So you must verify this thoroughly until you are certain; then you can start the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And recognize dislocations when it is tilted towards the shoulder blade, and you will see a clear difference between the diseased and healthy shoulder, and you will find their distinct variability among each other.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	You will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder. From the shoulder blade to the armpit, the head of the shoulder behaves as if it were a socket; and the patient cannot bring their hand back to their nose, nor move it with any movements;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	Also, if it is dislocated upwards and not completely hidden, for you will clearly find it at the armpit;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this way of dislocation must merely be to reposition it, when it is new or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the ministers lift their hand from the disease up, then place their thumbs under the joint, and lift the joint to its full height at the top of its position; and the ministers lift their hand and extend it upwards, putting it underneath; if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it doesn't come as we have said within days, then the sick person should be bathed in warm water; and the practitioner should apply soothing warmth and relief, such as a decoction of garlic and fenugreek and milk thistle in water, and it should be applied.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then dress the sick person on their back, and place a piece of even wool underneath the joint, not too soft nor too hard, then put the heel of the foot on the piece, and lift the shoulder blade upward, and pull the hand towards the diseased area.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another minister pricks the back of his adversary's neck, so that he cannot move downwards; that shoulder returns now completely, and if you see that you reset it in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And it is that you make the space present .i., at home which should be larger than the adversary's; and is upright towards the costeit side, and pushes the shoulder onto the slope of the neck, and lifts the slope upwards, so that the adversary hangs in the ar.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another minister pulls the hand from the adversary's neck downwards towards the belly. And if the adversary is too light, then by no means bear any weight with him, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And you also reset it in another way: and that is to stick a long piece of charcoal in the ground, so that the head is balanced like one pistol, and should neither be too big nor too greasy;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then have the patient place their hand near the wound but with a shield under it, and let the limb stay as long as the length of the staff. Then extend your other hand down from above, forming, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if she doesn't return with all these things that we have said, then do this treatment: take one staff of two strong arms and four large rods which allow the head to easily enter from all sides, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie the staff with a shield underneath so it doesn't hurt the patient, then place the staff under the wound on the patient; and extend your arms along the staff as long as needed, and tie the brace onto the staff, and the arm at the hand's head, then put the arm on one of the pegs of the same size from below, and keep the hands down, and leave the body hanging on the other side: the joint will return to its place now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when she is in this condition, no matter how it may be, if you need to place a piece of equal thread over the joint, then apply plaster mixed with flour from the mill, along with incense and egg yolk oil over the entire shoulder and around it, then remove the thread when done applying, and tie the bandage over the plaster, and wrap your hand around her neck, and keep your hands in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he nibble a little bit, until the limbs are strengthened, for they will heal faster; and then nibble more after about five days or seven, and move them; and if it is firm and not softened, it has healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is loose because of moisture or for another reason, it is necessary to administer three applications of a cautery tool, as was explained in the chapter about cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint doesn't hold, and can't lift your arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is either cut, stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never properly set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocation around the buttocks and breasts, or behind, happens due to pushing and stretching of hands, and it can occur elsewhere; and treat as long as they are in order.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there are still pains in the member and late movements, then one should bathe their body many times, until those pains ease away, and it returns to its original condition.
de la dislocation dou coute	From the dislocation of the shoulder

Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez. Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie. Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation from inside is that when you join the diseased leg with the healthy one, it becomes longer, and the diseased knee opens further than the healthy one, and the diseased knee cannot bend to touch the fire.

And the signs for him who approaches beforehand, are that his leg is well according to its completion; yet, neither double nor walk without pain, and if you try to make them walk, they cannot do it before, and retain their urine, and swell the ankle, and when he walks, he walks on the heel.

And let them rest for three or four days, then release and place the plaster; and if you see that they are equal, tighten as before, and leave them for another three days; then release and allow them to walk properly until the limb is reinforced.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the shoulder joint dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder joint can be dislocated in three ways: to understand this is as follows, either internally or externally, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs for this are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and if they cannot reach their knee, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	And for the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit up straight, and if they can extend their leg, do so, and place your back on their thigh, and put their foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	Then take his knee in your palms, and draw it between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee joint; and some other attendants spread his feet as far as the knees return to their place. And the signs are that he has comfortably moved his leg slightly with respect to his thigh.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And place the plaster on, and allow the leg to be in line with the thigh, and join them together tightly for three or four days. Then release it; and do not move any part of the wound until the limbs are strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limbs are not yet properly aligned, apply strong extension therapy, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never completely dislocated and neither fully out of place, both inwards and outwards.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle swells, and it tries to move forward towards the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The readjustment is quick; you should gently stretch it with your hands when it's only dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated right away, you should have the patient sit upright, and hold them one and a half lengths of your body length by their leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull their foot towards you with your right hand and then with the left twice, then extend them upwards, and firmly hold their foot high;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this twice, as we have said, by gripping and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's well; if not, start the process again because it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return in this way, you should let the patient lie on their back on the ground, and place one stick firmly in the ground between their buttocks, and tie cloths around them so that they don't hurt the patient.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then the ministers burn the leg, and other ministers extend his feet to his hands or two inches below the knee, as he ties them above the neck of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then extend each minister equally, and have the helper placed between the legs of the patient to hold the patient when they are extended.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then put the dislocated joint in equal position at your hands, and other ministers burn the healthy leg at its base; the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is in the right position, put on the plaster and fasten it up, then tighten properly, bind the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle bone, so the bandages should not be too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then leave it for two days or three, and if the patient sweats, remove them; then release it on the third day or the fourth, and continue to guide the person for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And even if he goes beyond this, it doesn't mean that he won't dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if pus comes out at the incision site, it is necessary that you soothe it, just as we have said in other places, while it remains clean.
des dois	Of the cautery made with fire, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, if they can be properly stretched like in manual work, it's a simple task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocations are in no bone of back or feet, it's necessary that you make the patient lie down on their full back or on the table completely straight, and place your foot on what opens from these joints, then press with your foot firmly until they regain consciousness.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when they are even and do not open anything, place under the foot of the patient a board with two shoulder heads, then hold them in form, and leave him for three days, then release him; and make him rest until he is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	regarding injuries and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When an injury comes with a dislocation, and one needs to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the treatment, and if you are knowledgeable in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and if you are compassionate and merciful but patient, do not be reckless;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And at the beginning of things that soothe, remove a hot abscess, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope for recovery;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, then reset the limb in its place immediately, so that the abscesses are removed and heal.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is in place, administer remedies that soothe abscesses and heal wounds, according to what is necessary, with drying ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if there's a break due to the dislocation, and small bones are exposed, set them back in place, and do as we have said for simple illnesses.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	And protect yourself from entering the path of fear, according to what I have said, because this is worth doing in accordance with your Creator, and for the knowledge that you arm yourself and guard your body. Amen
